201506	766	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And there was some concern about a “tightening tantrum,” in which there is fallout from spikes in market volatility and capital flows.	13	1
201506	767	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	But the general assessment was that US policy normalization has been well telegraphed.	13	1
201506	768	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In addition, the taper tantrum of 2013 has served as a warning to leaders in the region, and they appear to be prepared to cope with any resulting effects on capital flows.	13	1
201506	769	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	We also found policymakers in China ready and willing to do whatever it takes to ensure strong growth in that country.	13	1
201506	770	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	For example, the indications that their growth projection might slip from 7.1 percent to 7.0 percent fostered consideration of additional stimulatory policy initiatives.	13	1
201506	771	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Indeed, the central Chinese government recently reversed a policy intended to add discipline to local government borrowing when it became concerned that this would damp infrastructure spending and growth.	13	1
201506	772	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	With regard to the US labor market, I expect the unemployment rate to fall below my 5.2 percent estimate of the natural rate by the end of the year.	13	1
201506	773	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	The standard U-3 measure of unemployment is aligned with other measures of slack as well, such as the broader U-4 and U-5 measures of labor market underutilization, which include people not actively searching for a job but available and interested in work.	13	1
201506	774	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	It’s actually interesting to see that, unlike earlier points in the recession and the recovery, U-4 and U-5 are no longer indicating greater slack than does U-3.	13	1
201506	775	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Indeed, using all the available data back to 1994, the current levels of U-4 and U-5 are identical to their historical averages for all months when the unemployment rate was at its current level of 5½ percent.	13	1
201506	776	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In contrast, the broadest U-6 measure of labor underutilization, which includes involuntary part-time workers, is about 1 percentage point higher than its average during months where U-3 was 5½ percent.	13	1
201506	777	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	My staff has examined the factors behind the elevated level of involuntary part-time jobs using state-level data.	13	1
201506	778	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	They find that much of the earlier increase in involuntary part-time jobs was explained by cyclical factors.	13	1
201506	779	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	However, they also uncovered some evidence of an important role for changes in the compositional features of the labor market, most notably the industry job shares and workforce demographics, that help explain the elevated level of involuntary part-time jobs today.	13	1
201506	780	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Indeed, these more persistent compositional factors account for much of the currently elevated number of involuntary part-timers beyond what one would expect on the basis of the 5½ percent unemployment rate.	13	1
201506	781	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Based on these findings, I conclude that the signal about slack given by U-6 is roughly in line with the evidence from the other measures of unemployment.	13	1
201506	782	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Further supporting evidence for there being a relatively modest degree of slack in the labor market is provided by the pickup in several measures of employee compensation, as mentioned earlier.	13	1
201506	783	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	The historical pattern is that nominal wage growth doesn’t really shift up until late in the recovery when the economy is approaching full employment.	13	1
201506	784	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And we’re, I think, getting to that stage now, and I think the compensation data are following the usual script in that regard.	13	1
201506	785	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	To sum up, my view is that numerous indicators point to some slack still being out there in the labor market, but likely no more than implied by the U-3 unemployment measure.	13	1
201506	786	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	With regard to inflation, I continue to anticipate that we will achieve our 2 percent inflation objective by the end of next year.	13	1
201506	787	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Certainly the stars are aligned for such a return, with oil prices edging higher, the dollar edging lower, and, importantly, full employment in sight.	13	1
201506	788	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Still, there is no question that we are in a global environment of very low inflation, and the actual data—inflation data—have yet to provide a clear signal that we are on track.	13	1
201506	789	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	So, for me, the key outstanding issue for policy is obtaining more confidence that inflation will make a timely return to 2 percent, and for that we will just need to see more data.	13	1

201506	793	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201506	794	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	My forecast does not have a “Golden State” adjustment factor, so it’s not quite as optimistic as President Williams’s.	13	1
201506	795	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	My SEP submission does not differ significantly from the Tealbook forecast and has not changed much from the March meeting, although I assume in this submission that the first tightening will be in the fourth quarter, not in September.	13	1
201506	796	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The biggest change from my previous submission is the marking down of 2015 real GDP growth to reflect the weak data we received for the first half of this year.	13	1
201506	797	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The data bearing on second-quarter real GDP growth have been surprisingly weak after allowing for the fact that the bounceback from the array of first-quarter special factors is likely artificially elevating reported growth for the current quarter.	13	1
201506	798	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	If the Tealbook adjustment to transitory factors is accurate, second-quarter growth adjusted for these factors may fall short of potential growth.	13	1
201506	799	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Put differently, the weather and other transitory factors only partly explain the weakness in the first half of the year, since data both before and after the winter storms have remained relatively weak.	13	1
201506	800	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Although the May retail sales numbers and revisions to earlier months provide some comfort that consumption will not be particularly weak this quarter, it remains slower than I would expect on the basis of its strong fundamental drivers.	13	1
201506	801	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The apparent desire of consumers to save rather than spend the windfall generated by lower oil prices puts at risk the consumer-led recovery that I and many others foresaw at the time of the March SEP submission.	13	1
201506	802	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The May payroll employment report provides further evidence of healing labor markets.	13	1
201506	803	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, I am cautious about the labor market outlook for several reasons.	13	1
201506	804	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The unemployment rate has, at least for the moment, leveled off at 5½ percent—basically unchanged since February.	13	1
201506	805	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Under my projection of only moderate growth in the second half of this year, we will likely return only gradually to my 5 percent estimate of the full-employment unemployment rate.	13	1
201506	806	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	It is notable that the labor market conditions index shown in the Tealbook indicates only modest growth in the first quarter and is negative for the average of the first two months of this quarter.	13	1
201506	807	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Although I would not take too literally the magnitude of the change in labor market conditions implied by the LMCI, I would interpret the index as indicating some slowdown in labor market conditions relative to last year.	13	1
201506	808	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	And, of course, the labor market conditions would likely slow further if we do not see the expected pickup in growth in the second half of this year.	13	1
201506	809	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Progress on returning inflation to its 2 percent target over the forecast horizon remains disappointing.	13	1
201506	810	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Core PCE inflation over the past year is currently at 1.2 percent, well below what many of us were forecasting at the beginning of this year.	13	1
201506	811	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Sifting through the various indicators of price pressures provides little evidence that prices have yet begun trending toward 2 percent.	13	1
201506	812	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	It is still possible that transitory factors, such as exchange rate and energy pass-through, are playing a noticeable role, and that once these factors fade, progress toward our inflation goal will occur.	13	1
201506	813	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, I place some weight on the possibility that the current low inflation readings reflect an anchoring of inflation expectations below our 2 percent target.	13	1
201506	814	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Another possibility is that the equilibrium unemployment rate is running below my estimate of 5 percent.	13	1
201506	815	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In light of the uncertainty surrounding the inflation outlook, policy guidance should not just rely, as it does now, on being “reasonably confident that inflation will move back to its forecasts that indicate such a return is in train.	13	1
201506	816	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In a sense, that is why we have moved to data dependence in our policy decisions.	13	1
201506	817	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	To be specific, becoming reasonably confident that we will trend toward 2 percent inflation requires evidence that core PCE inflation is closer to the 1½ percent growth that we had been expecting earlier this year, that real growth is growing faster than we have seen so far in the first half of this year, and that the growth is sufficiently high to produce a further tightening in labor markets.	13	1
201506	818	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	There have been significant benefits to being as patient as we have been to date.	13	1
201506	819	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Broader measures of unemployment have continued to improve, though they still remain elevated.	13	1
201506	820	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Tighter labor markets are beginning to provide modest evidence of a gradual increase in nominal wages and compensation.	13	1
201506	821	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	And we have not tightened financial conditions at a time when Europe is going through a particularly difficult time.	13	1
201506	822	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201506	824	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Lockhart.	13	1
201506	825	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201506	826	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	My base-case economic and policy outlook has growth resuming in the second quarter and accelerating to around 3 percent in the third and fourth quarters.	13	1
201506	827	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	My base case has job gains continuing at a healthy rate in excess of 200,000 per month and other labor market data indicating that tightening continues.	13	1
201506	828	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The base case has household spending picking up in the second quarter, coincident with an acceleration of wage and income growth.	13	1
201506	829	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	And, finally, my base case has core inflation at least stable, near-term inflation data showing slight firming, and inflation expectations remaining stable.	13	1
201506	830	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I have been processing both anecdotal inputs and incoming data using this simple test: Does the information, on balance, support my outlook or cast doubt on it?	13	1
201506	831	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Although there are some encouraging signs, not quite enough conclusive evidence has yet accumulated to give me adequate comfort that my outlook is achievable.	13	1
201506	832	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	So let me survey quickly some of the information I have put through this test.	13	1
201506	833	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Our contacts with the business community in my District over the intermeeting period pointed to a somewhat slow, but not unsatisfactory, second quarter.	13	1
201506	834	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Sentiment about the pace of business activity in the second half remains positive, with a hint of caution.	13	1
201506	835	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The St Louis and Atlanta Bank boards met together last week.	13	1
201506	836	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	And President Bullard may have different “takeaways,” but I noted that most directors in attendance indicated they believe the first-quarter weakness was an anomaly, but most—or a majority—would not entirely dismiss the possibility of a prolonged period of weak growth.	13	1
201506	837	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Those contacts in my District exposed to overseas demand and the dollar exchange value continue to report negative effects.	13	1
201506	838	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Our port contacts reported a sharp drop-off in export traffic.	13	1
201506	839	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Because of the importance of strong consumer spending to my forecast, I have been especially attentive in this recent cycle to reports on the consumer.	13	1
201506	840	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Last week’s positive retail spending report was a step in the right direction.	13	1
201506	841	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Contacts tied to the new car market continue to report exceptionally brisk sales, along with strong production activity.	13	1
201506	842	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	But soft-goods retailers continue to see lackluster sales growth, and many expressed disappointment that this year’s lower gasoline prices have yet to translate into a stronger appetite for nondurables.	13	1
201506	843	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	At the same time, we heard a belief on the part of casual dining and tourism contacts that lower fuel prices are contributing to some strengthening in their sectors.	13	1
201506	844	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The picture that comes through is one of a discriminating consumer who is spending very selectively.	13	1
201506	845	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Perhaps the most significant change of sentiment since the previous meeting relates to labor markets.	13	1
201506	846	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The assessment of our District contacts of labor market conditions moved this cycle strongly toward a general description of labor markets as “tight.”	13	1
201506	847	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	This view was broad based.	13	1
201506	848	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	We heard more mentions than in the recent past of firms having to boost starting wages to attract new hires, make counteroffers to retain employees, and compete with more liberal benefits and bonus incentives.	13	1
201506	849	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Those not yet experiencing these broad pressures noted the inevitability of rising wages.	13	1
201506	850	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Overall, I interpret the weight of recent anecdotal inputs from my District contacts as supporting my base case.	13	1
201506	851	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I won’t belabor the evidence of all of the recent incoming data, but I’ll mention those that have most influenced my reading of the economy.	13	1
201506	852	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Early in this quarter, the Federal Reserve Bank of Atlanta’s GDPNow tracking model was showing second-quarter GDP growth more consistent with the weak first quarter than the hoped-for bounceback.	13	1
201506	853	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	With the recent trade, jobs, and retail sales reports, our tracker rose markedly and now has second-quarter growth just short of 2 percent.	13	1
201506	854	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	This rise is encouraging, but we still have second-quarter growth in our forecast at this point at around a 2 percent annual pace—well below what I was looking for.	13	1
201506	855	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	The first half still looks weak.	13	1
201506	856	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	A wage growth measure recently constructed by my staff that builds on the methods of the Federal Reserve Bank of San Francisco indicates that nominal wage growth is picking up.	13	1
201506	857	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	We conclude that the improved ECI numbers posted in the first quarter will likely move even higher this quarter.	13	1
201506	858	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	These indications of wage growth, combined with our latest anecdotal feedback on the subject, form the main reason I believe my base case remains on track.	13	1
201506	859	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	Employing a dashboard approach to inflation, I’ve been somewhat encouraged by indications that shorter-horizon PCE and CPI measures have been firming from their 12-month readings.	13	1
201506	860	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I’ve noted that the recent pickup in the Federal Reserve Bank of Dallas’ trimmed mean PCE measure and the market-based core PCE number.	13	1
201506	861	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I take the recent data in general as encouraging.	13	1
201506	862	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	As regards my official forecast for this meeting, I lowered my 2015 growth estimate to account for the soft first-quarter number but otherwise haven’t materially changed the projection from that I submitted in March.	13	1
201506	863	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	My growth projection is ½ percentage point above the revised Tealbook outlook for the year and about 25 basis points higher in 2016 and 2017.	13	1
201506	864	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I have inflation running about 25 basis points above the Tealbook over the forecast horizon.	13	1
201506	865	2015-06-17	meeting	LOCKHART	I have the risks to my outlook as balanced for inflation but to the downside for growth, reflecting in part the global economy.	13	1

201506	941	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Our projections of GDP growth, unemployment, and core inflation, prepared by macroeconomists at the Federal Reserve Bank of Dallas, are within the central tendency of the latest SEP projections for every year between 2015 and 2017, and in the longer run.	13	1

201506	943	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	It’s our belief that accommodative financial conditions will drive the unemployment rate past the natural rate late this year to reach 2 percent and low and shrinking labor market slack, trimmed mean PCE inflation rises to 1¾ percent by early 2016 and averages 2 percent for the year as a whole.	13	1
201506	944	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Our inflation forecasting approach has done well over the course of the recovery.	13	1
201506	945	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	In particular, it has not systematically overpredicted inflation as one would expect if longer-term inflation expectations had slipped below 2 percent or if the unemployment rate had been understating slack.	13	1

201506	959	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	For example, the CEO of United Airlines reported that business travel was weak at all the major carriers.	13	1
201506	960	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	And I also heard a number of comments that, taking into account the slow growth in demand, CEOs in general currently do not foresee much need, over the next 6 to 12 months, for ramping up capital investment or hiring.	13	1
201506	961	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	But the moods seem more like continued caution than actual anxiety regarding any slowing.	13	1
201506	962	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Indeed, I did hear a few relatively optimistic reports.	13	1
201506	963	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	One came from Caterpillar, who said some of their oilfield equipment customers had become more positive about their ability to operate profitably now that the price of oil seems to be stabilizing at around $60 per barrel.	13	1
201506	964	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	And the auto sector is pretty upbeat.	13	1
201506	965	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Demand has been strong, causing Ford and some others to push up their light vehicle sales forecast for the year to around 17 million units, which is a bit above the Tealbook forecast.	13	1
201506	966	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	But if we are looking for boosts to consumer spending over the next few years, it probably won’t be coming from autos.	13	1
201506	967	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	The sector already has contributed very strongly to this recovery.	13	1
201506	968	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	It’s running at a high level, and at 17 million units, it’s hard to imagine that there can be much upside vehicle demand that’s going to add to GDP growth.	13	1
201506	969	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	With regard to inflation, I didn’t hear any meaningful new reports of wage or price pressures from my contacts.	13	1
201506	970	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Indeed, steel and other commodity prices remained low, which could present some downside risk to the inflation outlook.	13	1
201506	971	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	My own forecast is pretty similar to what I’ve been hearing from my business contacts.	13	1
201506	972	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	I’m cautiously optimistic about better growth and continued labor market improvements in the quarters ahead.	13	1
201506	973	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Of course, Federal Reserve forecasting credibility has taken a beating throughout this recovery, as our optimism in January has given way to much more subdued actual growth outcomes, although I’m looking forward to the public pronouncement of President Williams’s seasonal adjustment on the first-quarter GDP data—maybe that will change things.	13	1
201506	974	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	This forecasting reality is another reason to temper our more enthusiastic projections.	13	1
201506	975	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	And on inflation, I’m not optimistic at all.	13	1
201506	976	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	I don’t see inflation rising to target in anything like a reasonable time frame.	13	1
201506	977	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Turning to the specifics, our projection of GDP has growth running between 2½ and 2¾ percent over the remainder of this year and next.	13	1
201506	978	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Our assumptions regarding potential output growth are somewhat stronger than the Tealbook’s, so this GDP path translates into a similar reduction in resource gaps.	13	1
201506	979	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	And by the end of 2016, we have the unemployment rate down to around 5 percent, which is my current assessment of the natural rate.	13	1
201506	980	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	On the inflation front, the apparent stabilization of the dollar and oil prices have been favorable developments, as have been the recent increases in TIPS breakevens, although I would note that breakevens still remain well below their normal and year-ago levels.	13	1
201506	981	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	However, I’ve become less sanguine about the message from survey measures of long- term inflation expectations.	13	1
201506	982	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	For sure, the SPF 10-year outlook for PCE inflation has been remarkably stable despite many years of low actual inflation.	13	1
201506	983	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	One interpretation is that these professionals simply write down our announced 2 percent target for 10 years out.	13	1
201506	984	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	But there is another inflation measure that the SPF regularly reports—namely, the 10-year CPI forecast—and this tells a different story.	13	1
201506	985	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	This 10-year CPI forecast has become more volatile since the crisis, but generally it has trended down.	13	1
201506	986	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	And on net over the past three years, it’s fallen more than 30 basis points and is now about 2.1 percent.	13	1
201506	987	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Given the usual 35 to 40 basis point wedge between PCE and CPI, the two SPF 10-year forecasts seem at odds, and that is troubling.	13	1
201506	988	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	What’s more, this downward drift in the SPF long-run CPI outlook has an important influence on the inflation forecast produced by the Federal Reserve Bank of Chicago’s DSGE model.	13	1
201506	989	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Our model includes a time-varying unobserved inflation benchmark.	13	1
201506	990	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	This benchmark acts as a long-run attractor for the path of inflation.	13	1
201506	991	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	As I understand it, the Tealbook inflation forecast is informed by a similar type of stochastic trend.	13	1
201506	992	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	The 10-year SPF CPI forecast is an important factor informing the Chicago model’s inflation benchmark.	13	1
201506	993	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	However, there are many shocks that can cause the benchmark to deviate from the SPF.	13	1
201506	994	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	In other words, there’s plenty of scope in the model for the downward drift in the SPF CPI expectations to be explained by shocks that do not affect benchmark inflation and, hence, would not show through in the model’s longer-run inflation forecast.	13	1
201506	995	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	However, that does not turn out to be the case right now.	13	1
201506	996	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	The model currently interprets the SPF 10-year CPIs and other incoming data as a string of mostly negative shocks to the inflation benchmark that have pulled this measure down almost 25 basis points over the past couple of years.	13	1
201506	997	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	These shocks have long-lasting effects in the model.	13	1
201506	998	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	As a result, the model’s PCE inflation forecast is significantly below our 2 percent target for many years to come.	13	1
201506	999	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	According to this analysis, the low inflation we’ve experienced the past several years has already fed through into public perceptions, which is making it more difficult for us to achieve our inflation objective.	13	1
201506	1000	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	On the basis of this DSGE work, projections from other models that we’ve run, and commentary from my business contacts, I’m having a hard time writing down a forecast that gets inflation returning to target within a reasonable time frame.	13	1
201506	1001	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	My projection has PCE inflation getting back to just 1.7 percent by the end of 2017, and I can see important downside risks to this forecast.	13	1
201506	1002	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201506	1015	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	Our survey of District business contacts across all sectors yielded a diffusion index of contacts reporting better versus worse conditions that improved substantially in June to 36 percent from the near 20 percent level seen in March and April.	13	1

201506	1017	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	For the year ending in April, District payrolls grew at 1.3 percent.	13	1

201506	1020	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	Regional employment growth has been slower than the US average in recovery since the 1980s.	13	1
201506	1021	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	Over the first four months of the year, the Fourth District unemployment rate has been stable at around 5.2 percent, lower than the national rate of 5.5 percent.	13	1
201506	1022	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	The responses from nearly 100 firms that the Federal Reserve Bank of Cleveland staff contacted as part of the Federal Reserve special survey on hiring plans and compensation indicate that demand for workers remains solid—63 percent of our respondents expect to increase employment over the next 12 months.	13	1

201506	1026	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	In terms of compensation, 66 percent of contacts who reported increasing starting wages are doing so only in selected occupations, including engineering and IT.	13	1

201506	1030	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	For the national economy, my read of the incoming data since our most recent meeting is that the data are consistent with the first-quarter weakness having been largely due to temporary factors, including the severe winter weather, the West Coast port strike, and seasonal adjustment issues.	13	1

201506	1032	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	The effect of other factors—like the earlier sharp drop in oil prices, which has caused the energy and mining sector to cut back activity, and the appreciation of the dollar, which has affected manufacturing and trade—are not likely to reverse quickly.	13	1
201506	1033	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	But over the last few months, energy prices have stabilized and the appreciation of the dollar has slowed, and this should help lessen the drags on these sectors.	13	1

201506	1045	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	But I continue to see growth picking up over the remainder of the year to about 3 percent late this year and next before slowing to my estimate of trend growth in 2017.	13	1

201506	1048	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	Research by the Federal Reserve Bank of Cleveland staff shows that across a range of statistical models, large reductions in oil and gasoline prices should give a sizable boost to consumer spending, although the timing of such a response varies depending on the model.	13	1
201506	1049	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	With above-trend growth later this year and next, I expect further improvements in labor markets, with the unemployment rate falling to 5.2 percent by the end of this year.	13	1

201506	1051	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	This means the economy will no longer be underutilizing labor resources.	13	1

201506	1053	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	It’s also consistent with research by my staff that estimated the longer-run normal level of unemployment using five different conceptual approaches and found that the degree of underutilization of labor resources has been significantly reduced.	13	1
201506	1054	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	The news on inflation over the intermeeting period was positive.	13	1

201506	1056	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	The Federal Reserve Bank of Cleveland’s inflation nowcast has headline PCE inflation rebounding from a minus 2 percent annual rate in the first quarter to 1.9 percent in the second quarter, and core PCE inflation moving up from 0.8 percent to 1.4 percent.	13	1
201506	1057	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	The Federal Reserve Bank of Cleveland’s median CPI rate has remained near 2.2 percent for the past seven months despite sharp movements in headline inflation rates and some softening in core inflation.	13	1
201506	1058	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	After dipping earlier this year, the Federal Reserve Bank of Cleveland’s 10-year inflation expectations edged up further in May to the levels seen last year, and survey measures of long-run inflation expectations have remained essentially unchanged.	13	1
201506	1059	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	The combination of stable inflation expectations, stabilizing oil prices, my forecast of above-trend growth, and further improvement in labor markets makes me reasonably confident that inflation will gradually return to our 2 percent target over the medium run by late 2016 or early 2017.	13	1
201506	1060	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	As I have discussed at earlier meetings, there is considerable uncertainty associated with any inflation forecast, including my own.	13	1
201506	1061	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	But based on Federal Reserve Bank of Cleveland staff work, I do not see that uncertainty as being exceptionally elevated.	13	1
201506	1062	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	This is also consistent with the Board staff’s view, as indicated in Tealbook, Book A, on page 67.	13	1
201506	1063	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	My projection depends on appropriate policy.	13	1
201506	1064	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	In my view, we are very near or already at full employment, and I am reasonably confident that inflation will gradually return to our goal of 2 percent over the medium run.	13	1
201506	1065	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	So an economic case can be made for increasing the federal funds rate from essentially zero at this meeting.	13	1
201506	1066	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	But, as we haven’t prepared the markets and the public for that, I wouldn’t view it as appropriate policy.	13	1
201506	1067	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	Instead, my projection incorporates liftoff in the third quarter and a gradual rise in interest rates thereafter throughout the forecast horizon.	13	1

201506	1069	2015-06-17	meeting	MESTER	Consumer and business spending may fail to pick up.	13	1

201506	1079	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	13	1
201506	1080	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201506	1081	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	In the midst of what looks like a weak first half for the US economy, we think that the data have, on balance, surprised to the upside over the last several weeks.	13	1
201506	1082	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	This gives us confidence that the economy will bounce back in the coming quarters in terms of GDP growth.	13	1
201506	1083	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	We think that measured GDP growth will average about 3 percent over the last three quarters of 2015, and that the unemployment rate will fall below 5 percent.	13	1
201506	1084	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	We continue to view the staff forecast for unemployment as not credible.	13	1
201506	1085	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	It calls for an unemployment rate at the end of 2017, two and a half years from today, just three-tenths lower than what it is today.	13	1
201506	1086	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	That’s more pessimistic on this dimension than the Blue Chip.	13	1
201506	1087	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	We think a more reasonable forecast calls for further cyclical improvement in unemployment and, indeed, in the associated labor market conditions index as well.	13	1
201506	1088	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	In the two expansions in the 1990s and 2000s, unemployment reached much lower levels.	13	1
201506	1089	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Those expansions arguably featured much less monetary policy accommodation than we have in train today.	13	1
201506	1090	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Anecdotal reports from around the Eighth District suggest that businesses remain generally optimistic for the remainder of this year.	13	1
201506	1091	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	A major hotel chain reported that the outlook for the travel and tourism industry is upbeat.	13	1
201506	1092	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	The furniture industry in northern Mississippi is expanding.	13	1
201506	1093	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	In the Louisville zone of the Eighth District, wages have increased 3½ percent from one year ago.	13	1
201506	1094	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	The District’s hiring plan survey indicates that two-thirds of businesses looking for new employees are raising starting salaries compared with a year ago.	13	1
201506	1095	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	These and other anecdotal reports, including those at the joint St Louis–Atlanta board meeting, give us confidence that the underlying growth in the US economy is relatively satisfactory, and that residual seasonality or other measurement error accounts for much of the apparent weakness in real GDP growth during the first half of 2015.	13	1
201506	1096	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	This view is consistent with the relatively strong labor market reports we have received so far this year.	13	1
201506	1097	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Despite my relatively optimistic view of the US economy, the Committee has emphasized the data dependency of policy, and therefore I think it has been entirely appropriate for financial market participants and this Committee to push back the likely date of liftoff in response.	13	1
201506	1098	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	My only comment in this regard is that this effect should appropriately work in the reverse direction as well.	13	1
201506	1099	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	In particular, data that surprise us in a positive sense compared with the relatively dour staff forecast might be expected to pull forward the date of liftoff in order to maintain the appropriate level of policy accommodation.	13	1
201506	1100	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Indeed, we expect even modestly strong economic data to cause just such a reaction in financial markets, and we think the Committee should be prepared to move in such a circumstance.	13	1
201506	1101	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	The remainder of my comments focus on r*.	13	1
201506	1102	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I began arguing last year that relatively small unemployment and inflation gaps suggest that the US economy is close to normal in terms of our target variables.	13	1
201506	1103	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	In particular, unemployment at 5.5 percent is not too far from estimates of a reasonable long-run level—certainly much closer than it has been over the past five years.	13	1
201506	1104	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Similarly, an appropriately smoothed measure of inflation, like the year-over-year Federal Reserve Bank of Dallas trimmed mean, shows a value of about 1.6 percent, just four- tenths below the Committee’s stated target.	13	1
201506	1105	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Both of these gaps are likely to become even smaller in the quarters ahead.	13	1
201506	1106	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I have calculated that, in terms of how close we are to our goals using a quadratic objective function, we are closer in recent quarters than we have been about 90 percent of the time during the postwar era.	13	1
201506	1107	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	By this measure, we are doing very well indeed with respect to our target variables.	13	1
201506	1108	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	If we put these relatively small gaps into standard Taylor-type rules, recommended policy rates tend to be much higher than today’s policy setting, as shown on page 2 of Tealbook, Book B.	13	1
201506	1109	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	These rules have served as a description of relatively good monetary policy in the past, so why deviate today?	13	1
201506	1110	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	One idea is that the intercept term in a Taylor-type rule, r*, is not constant but is instead time varying, and that today’s value is particularly low.	13	1
201506	1111	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	This might justify a low policy rate even in the face of relatively small unemployment and inflation gaps.	13	1
201506	1112	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I want to make two points on this.	13	1
201506	1113	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Number one, is this the argument we want to make?	13	1
201506	1114	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Number two, how should we measure r*?	13	1
201506	1115	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	On the first question, whether this is the argument we want to make, I interpret the nature of the argument to be that today’s zero policy rate is not providing as much accommodation as one might otherwise think, because r* is, in fact, time-varying and happens to be low today.	13	1
201506	1116	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Yet, in other portions of the Committee rhetoric, we have argued that a zero interest rate policy, combined with a large balance sheet, is in fact providing a large and appropriate amount of accommodation to combat perceived headwinds inhibiting US macroeconomic progress.	13	1
201506	1117	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	From that perspective, I see it as a bit of a cross-purpose to suggest that, in fact, our policy is not as powerful as it would appear according to standard calculations.	13	1
201506	1118	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	On the second question of how to measure r*, a few of you noted the recent Federal Reserve Bank of St Louis Fed blog post by Bill Dupor.	13	1
201506	1119	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	The idea of the post was to calculate r* using various ideas in standard theory on benchmark real interest rates and compare them to the Laubach-Williams calculation.	13	1
201506	1120	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	The alternative calculations tend to suggest that, while r* may be lower today than it has been historically, it is not so low as to suggest that the Committee is not being accommodative with its current policy setting.	13	1
201506	1121	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	This may be one way to reconcile the compelling idea that r* should be time varying with the idea that the ZIRP is likely very accommodative by conventional metrics.	13	1
201506	1122	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201506	1162	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I’d like to close with a comment on what seems to be the latent variable du jour— namely, the equilibrium real rate.	13	1
201506	1163	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Maybe it’s the latent variable of the year, I don’t know.	13	1
201506	1164	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Several participants last time urged more research on r*, and there’s been a lot of commentary on r* today.	13	1
201506	1165	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	It’s hard to object to more research, but I’m not sure we should get our hopes up.	13	1
201506	1166	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I’ll point out that, by itself, saying the federal funds rate is low because the equilibrium real rate is low is sort of empty.	13	1
201506	1167	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Robert Tetlow presented pictures in which our federal funds rate’s deviations from a Taylor rule prescription were attributed to the residual.	13	1
201506	1168	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Anything you attribute to a residual in a Taylor rule can be handed off to the constant term, the r* term, so an equivalent interpretation is our own individual r* efforts.	13	1
201506	1169	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Presumably, we set the funds rate to what we believe it should be, and, presumably, we all now think that it should be below where you’d expect it to be, on the basis of current values of inflation and output gaps, and historical correlations between real rates and inflation and output gaps.	13	1
201506	1170	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	But virtually any setting for the funds rate can be rationalized by assuming a shift in the intercept term for the correlations between the real funds rate and output–inflation gaps.	13	1
201506	1171	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	So, by itself, it doesn’t have much content, in the absence of independent information brought to bear about what the equilibrium funds rate is.	13	1
201506	1172	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	That requires using identifying assumptions, either by applying a statistical model or applying some economic theory.	13	1
201506	1173	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Now, those estimates are going to be model dependent, the point President Williams made.	13	1
201506	1174	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	There are only a few of these out there right now, but, personally, I’d be surprised if the procedures yielded estimates of the equilibrium real rate that were very closely aligned.	13	1
201506	1175	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	In fact, President Williams’s comment was essentially pointing out the discrepancy between the Laubach-Williams model estimate and the staff’s estimate.	13	1
201506	1176	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Some statistical methods for parameterizing the real rate process imply that the long-term real trend rate has drifted down—that is, the level has drifted down permanently.	13	1
201506	1177	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	But there are other parameterizations that are equally plausible and that imply that the long-run trend rate hasn’t fallen much over the last couple of decades, and what we’re in the midst of is a transition dynamic back to the long-run trend.	13	1
201506	1178	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I think this exactly describes, to some extent, the difference between President Williams and the staff.	13	1
201506	1179	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Now, this isn’t to say that such exercises are going to be useless.	13	1
201506	1180	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	It just says that they’re not going to be terribly enlightening unless we are exceptionally clear about the nature of the underlying identification assumptions that drive the difference in results.	13	1
201506	1181	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	One last observation.	13	1
201506	1182	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	This is a personal peeve—I think this terminology is terrible.	13	1
201506	1183	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	The notion of “equilibrium” used here corresponds to the idea of a system at rest, as in Newtonian physics, essentially, and within economics that usage has been outmoded for four or five decades now.	13	1
201506	1184	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201506	1256	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Kocherlakota.	13	1
201506	1257	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201506	1258	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m going to spend my time today on the inflation outlook.	13	1
201506	1259	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Many around this table have rightly expressed the desire to guard against the risk of model misspecification in formulating inflation forecasts.	13	1
201506	1260	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So to mitigate this risk, my staff and I went through a suite of inflation forecasting models in preparation for this meeting.	13	1
201506	1261	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	My summary of this survey is that the balance of risk to inflation remains very much to the downside.	13	1
201506	1262	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	More specifically, the outlook in Tealbook, Book A, is that inflation will remain below 2 percent until 2019.	13	1
201506	1263	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Survey of Professional Forecasters’ median outlook is that inflation will remain below 2 percent through its forecast horizon, which ends in 2017.	13	1
201506	1264	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	All three Federal Reserve System DSGE models predict that inflation will remain below 2 percent through their forecast horizons.	13	1
201506	1265	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	At the Minneapolis Reserve Bank, we have a purely statistical model that we use for forecasting purposes—by “purely statistical,” what I mean is, we don’t layer onto it presumptions of the credibility of our target or a Phillips curve relationship.	13	1
201506	1266	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	However, the model is allowed to detect those things in the last 30 years of data if it’s able to find them.	13	1
201506	1267	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That model’s modal projection is that inflation will never return to 2 percent.	13	1
201506	1268	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It simply is not able to find enough of the Phillips curve relationship in the data for the past 30 years or enough evidence of the credibility of our inflation target to warrant getting back to 2 percent inflation.	13	1
201506	1269	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So I count that as six different model- and judgment-based inflation forecasts.	13	1
201506	1270	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, I continue to favor market-based—as opposed to model-based—inflation outlooks as the basis for policy.	13	1
201506	1271	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I won’t drag you through the details there, but, again, market-based outlooks tell a similar low-inflation story over the medium term.	13	1
201506	1272	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, this stands in contrast to the forecast that Robert went through from the Summary of Economic Projections.	13	1
201506	1273	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Nearly two-thirds of the forecasts in the Committee have inflation back to 2 percent or more at the end of 2017.	13	1
201506	1274	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Some of you probably have access to models or information that lead you to forecast a more rapid return of inflation to target.	13	1
201506	1275	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If you’re able to do so, it would be great to share those sources of information and modeling with my staff.	13	1
201506	1276	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We’d be very interested in understanding how people were getting to different conclusions about where we stand on inflation.	13	1
201506	1277	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Some of you might be seeing the Phillips curve as having more slope than we do.	13	1
201506	1278	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	You might see the natural rate as being higher than we do—or Board staff do, for that matter.	13	1
201506	1279	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It would be interesting to understand why.	13	1
201506	1280	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It would be useful to share that.	13	1
201506	1281	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	At least here in Minneapolis, we would be very interested in understanding what leads others to see more inflationary pressures than we were able to find right now.	13	1
201506	1282	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, it’s often emphasized that there are standard errors associated with these point forecasts, and I agree with that.	13	1
201506	1283	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	These associated standard errors are quite large.	13	1
201506	1284	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In light of those standard errors, I think the right way to read them is as a simple summary statistic of the balance of risks for inflation over the medium term.	13	1
201506	1285	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That builds in a symmetry assumption of how those errors are affecting the outcomes of inflation.	13	1
201506	1286	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If I tell you a point forecast, we can basically see what the likelihood is of inflation being above 2 percent or below.	13	1
201506	1287	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The low point forecasts are telling us that the probability that inflation will return to 2 percent over the medium term is under 50 percent, arguably considerably so, but that depends on a little more judgment and digging deeper to see exactly what those numbers look like.	13	1
201506	1288	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, this is all about the medium term.	13	1
201506	1289	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think these medium-term forecasts do not provide the full picture of the relevant inflation risks.	13	1
201506	1290	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I see little risk of inflation being stuck at, say, 2½ percent over the next 10 years.	13	1
201506	1291	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Committee has the tools and the will to forestall this outcome.	13	1
201506	1292	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In contrast, I see considerable risk that the Committee’s actions could lead inflation to be stuck at, say, 1½ percent over the next 10 years.	13	1
201506	1293	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think this is consistent with some of the discussion that President Evans offered about the CPI forecast that we see in the Survey of Professional Forecasters.	13	1
201506	1294	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Certainly they’re not forecasting 1½ percent PCE inflation over the next 10 years, I’m not saying that, but there’s a distribution of possible outcomes.	13	1
201506	1295	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I just don’t think it’s plausible that we’re going to see 2½ percent over the next 10 years, but I think it is plausible that we could see 1½ percent over the next 10 years.	13	1
201506	1296	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I don’t sense a will or a desire to use the tools needed to forestall that latter outcome.	13	1
201506	1297	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	After all, if you look back, the FOMC’s choices have led annual PCE core inflation to run below 2 percent in every month since late 2008, with the exception of a few months in late 2011 and early 2012.	13	1
201506	1298	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Over the past two years, the Committee has continued on a course of removing accommodation.	13	1
201506	1299	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Go back to, say, May 2013.	13	1
201506	1300	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think we basically have been on a path of removing accommodation pretty much in the teeth of the troubling inflation forecast that I’ve just described.	13	1
201506	1301	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	These outcome-based data suggest that the FOMC views PCE inflation under 2 percent— even over very long periods of time—as being an acceptable outcome of monetary policy decisionmaking.	13	1
201506	1302	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	My assessment that the FOMC lacks the will or the tools to defend the inflation target from below seems to be shared by financial markets.	13	1
201506	1303	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The market-based five-year, five- year-forward measures of expected inflation declined sharply in the second half of last year.	13	1
201506	1304	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Some observers insisted at the time that this decline would prove temporary, and they might yet be proved right—time will tell, I guess.	13	1
201506	1305	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But the relevant metrics continue to remain low by historical standards.	13	1
201506	1306	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Even though we’ve seen very sharp reversals of nominal bond yields, the inflation breakevens remain low.	13	1
201506	1307	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So what?	13	1
201506	1308	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There’s nothing hugely scientific about an inflation target of 2 percent, right?	13	1
201506	1309	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Couldn’t we have a true inflation target of, say, 1½ percent even if we had a stated inflation target of 2 percent?	13	1
201506	1310	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think there’s a couple of answers one could give.	13	1
201506	1311	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	One is that, as a publicly accountable institution, presumably the outcomes we’re trying to achieve should match up with our stated goals, but let’s leave that aside.	13	1
201506	1312	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Let’s talk just about economics.	13	1
201506	1313	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The problem is that a lower inflation target will lead to worse real outcomes.	13	1
201506	1314	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If inflation breakevens are 1½ percent rather than 2 percent, then nominal yields would be 50 basis points lower on average.	13	1
201506	1315	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That means it will take a smaller shock to the natural real interest rate to hit the zero lower bound.	13	1
201506	1316	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Our tools in those circumstances are costly, especially with the size of the balance sheet that we’re currently maintaining.	13	1
201506	1317	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So our stays at the zero lower bound will lead to employment shortfalls, and those are why we should care—I think that’s easy for us all to see.	13	1
201506	1318	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If we want to meet our employment mandate in a more systematic fashion over the next decade, we should be doing more to buttress the credibility of our inflation target.	13	1
201506	1319	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’ll have more to say about how to best do so tomorrow, Madam Chair.	13	1
201506	1320	2015-06-17	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you.	13	1
201506	1321	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1
201506	1322	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	13	1
201506	1323	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201506	1324	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	My views can be characterized quite succinctly:  somewhat less confidence on growth and the further improvement in the labor market, and somewhat more confidence that inflation will return to our 2 percent objective over the medium term, assuming that the labor market continues to show further improvement.	13	1
201506	1325	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	On the growth side, I think I share the opinions of everyone else that the results have been somewhat disappointing, with growth in the first half now likely to come in at about a little bit over 1 percentage point.	13	1
201506	1326	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, some of this can be attributed to special factors:  the unseasonably cold, snowy winter; residual seasonal adjustment problems; transitory factors such as the sharp decline in oil and gas investment.	13	1
201506	1327	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	But all that said, it is disappointing, especially the weaker-than-expected trajectory of consumer spending.	13	1
201506	1328	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	However, last Thursday’s retail sales report for May was strong and there was a sizable upward revision in sales for March, so maybe some of the shortfall in consumer spending relative to expectations is already resolving itself.	13	1
201506	1329	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The consequences of the weakness in economic growth for the labor market had been much milder than one would expect—the circle squared by extraordinarily weak productivity growth—but I don’t believe that productivity growth is going to continue to be so poor.	13	1
201506	1330	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I suspect that payroll growth will slow markedly unless we get a meaningful pickup in the economic growth rate.	13	1
201506	1331	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, the good news is, I do expect the growth rate to pick up as some of the transitory negative influences on growth fade.	13	1
201506	1332	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I also take some cheer from the most recent set of employment reports because, with both hours worked being up sharply and wages rising more quickly, that implies we’ll see faster real disposable income growth, which should help sustain consumer spending.	13	1
201506	1333	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	However, I am nervous that if productivity growth returns to a more normal performance, the growth pickup could still not be strong enough to sustain the solid payroll gains that we’ve seen over the past year.	13	1
201506	1334	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So that’s the reason I’ve become slightly less confident that we’ll see further improvement in the labor market over the remainder of the year.	13	1
201506	1335	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, with respect to the poor productivity figures that we’ve seen recently—the 0 percent rise in non-farm business productivity over the last four quarters and the sharp decline in the fourth quarter and the first quarter—I asked this question of the staff, but I don’t have a good explanation either.	13	1
201506	1336	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	While it’s true that weak capital spending implies less capital deepening and this is having a negative consequence for productivity growth, that, I think, can only explain a portion of the slowdown over the past year.	13	1
201506	1337	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to the collapse of the past two quarters, I think this is even harder to explain.	13	1
201506	1338	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Even if innovations cease completely, and there’s certainly no evidence of that, productivity growth should keep expanding for quite some time, as earlier innovations diffuse throughout the economy.	13	1
201506	1339	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Perhaps real GDP growth rates will be revised up, or perhaps the poor performance is a temporary artifact that stems from businesses becoming more confident, hiring more workers, and then this translating into a particularly poor measure of productivity during this transitional period.	13	1
201506	1340	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	But whatever the source, I view this as a conundrum that does increase my uncertainty about the labor market outlook.	13	1
201506	1341	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to inflation, I am becoming more confident, subject to the labor market continuing to improve, that inflation will return toward our 2 percent objective over the medium term, and that this reflects three things.	13	1
201506	1342	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	First, we’re seeing further tightening of the labor market, and this seems to be translating to somewhat greater upward pressure on wages.	13	1
201506	1343	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, some of the transitory influences holding down inflation—namely, the earlier decline in oil and gas prices and the effect of the stronger dollar on nonpetroleum import prices—seems likely to dissipate.	13	1
201506	1344	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Evidence of a cyclical recovery in Europe and Japan has led to greater stability in the dollar, for example.	13	1
201506	1345	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Third, measures of inflation compensation have increased since earlier in the year, with the Board’s five-year, five-year-forward measure of inflation compensation rising by about 25 basis points from its low point in January.	13	1
201506	1346	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So what does this imply for monetary policy?	13	1
201506	1347	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Well, I’ll talk mostly about this tomorrow, but I still think we’re on track for liftoff in September.	13	1
201506	1348	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	I haven’t changed my SEP federal funds rate path from what I submitted at the March meeting:  two rate hikes of 25 basis points each in 2015—one in September and one in December—and I’ll have more to say on that tomorrow.	13	1
201506	1349	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Finally, how should we think about the sharp backup we’ve seen in bond yields recently?	13	1
201506	1350	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	My own view is that it’s warranted, and better now than later.	13	1
201506	1351	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The yields have been pulled down mainly by European QE, which had depressed bond term premiums, and soft Q1 activity measures that implied a potentially later liftoff of US monetary policy.	13	1
201506	1352	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Even with the rise to a little bit below 2.4 percent, 10-year Treasury yields are not particularly high, especially if you think we’re going to start a journey back to 3½ percent or so for the nominal federal funds rate later this year.	13	1
201506	1353	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Remember, after the taper tantrum we were at about 3 percent.	13	1
201506	1354	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The current yield curve implies a 10-year Treasury note yield in five years’ time of only about 3 percent.	13	1
201506	1355	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So even with this backup, we’re not really discounting a big rise in 10-year rates going forward.	13	1
201506	1356	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	To me, it’s better to have this occur in steps and away from the date of liftoff rather than one big jump around or following liftoff.	13	1
201506	1357	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So with the backup in the yields now, we have a yield curve that is quite a bit steeper than normal.	13	1
201506	1358	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Considerable tightening is already discounted in its shape, so I think that reduces the chance that we’ll see a really sharp rise in yields when we actually do lift off.	13	1
201506	1359	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	At least that’s my hope at this point.	13	1
201506	1360	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201506	1363	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201506	1364	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	In April, I—and I believe most of us around this table—were concerned that the underlying performance of the economy might be slowing more persistently than it had in the first quarter of 2014.	13	1
201506	1365	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	We were concerned in particular about slowing job gains, declining industrial output, and weakness in several spending categories.	13	1
201506	1366	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Most seriously, I was worried that the underlying, strongly positive thrust of economic activity— especially in the labor market, in which monthly increases in employment had averaged more than 260,000 in 2014—could be slowing.	13	1
201506	1367	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	And that fear was supported by the March increase in employment of only about 120,000.	13	1
201506	1368	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	It is worth emphasizing that the labor market has, for some time, been much stronger than the GDP data.	13	1
201506	1369	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Since early last year, the unemployment rate has declined more than 1 percentage point.	13	1
201506	1370	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	The difference in the behavior of output and employment has been puzzling since the start of the recovery, and it was particularly stark in the first quarters of 2014 and 2015, when GDP declined and, except in March 2015, hiring remained strong.	13	1
201506	1371	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	The staff generally takes the view that when the employment and GDP data appear inconsistent, the employment data are more likely to be accurate than the output data, which is to say that we should be putting more weight on the behavior of the employment data than on that implied by the GDP data if there is some error in the data, which is entirely possible.	13	1
201506	1372	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	The data coming in since our April meeting have reinforced the view that the weakness we saw in the first quarter was likely mostly transitory and should reassure us that the underlying strength of the labor market continues despite the March weakness.	13	1
201506	1373	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Consider the recent data.	13	1
201506	1374	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Real core retail sales have risen at an annual rate of 3½ percent so far this year, and auto sales have been extremely strong.	13	1
201506	1375	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Services data for the first quarter were also strong.	13	1
201506	1376	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Housing investment growth has stepped up considerably since the second half of last year.	13	1
201506	1377	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Specifically, residential investment is estimated to be rising at a 9 percent annual pace in the first half of this year, and that takes into account today’s data, which is up from a 3.5 percent gain in the second half of last year.	13	1
201506	1378	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	And we are finally beginning to see a pickup in compensation.	13	1
201506	1379	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	The 12-month change in the employment cost index has moved appreciably higher, which is in turn consistent with the ongoing improvements in the labor market.	13	1
201506	1380	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	The employment-to-population ratio has continued to rise this year, the participation rate has leveled out, the share of workers working part time for economic reasons has diminished further, and job openings have jumped.	13	1
201506	1381	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Anecdotal evidence reinforces these data.	13	1
201506	1382	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	In the Beige Book, most Districts reported improvements in the housing sector, with some describing the market as “very active” or “strong.”	13	1
201506	1383	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	And as noted in the summary of Districts’ hiring plans sent to us by Board staff members Glenn Follette and John Stevens, the number of respondents expecting to increase employment over the coming 12 months was as strong as it was in December and higher than it was in the preceding four annual inquiries.	13	1
201506	1384	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I’ve also been gathering my own anecdotes, mainly from the newspapers, which means I am far from keeping up with the presidents on this front.	13	1
201506	1385	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I’ve long been wishing to have an interlocutor, and I found one in an e-mail.	13	1
201506	1386	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Somebody wrote to me and said that his cousins in Hannibal, Missouri, which is in Jim Bullard’s District, had recently switched from riding in the rodeo to driving trucks for the local paint factory, which had boosted pay to attract workers.	13	1
201506	1387	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	My interlocutor remarked to his cousins that with their being drawn back into the workforce with higher wages, we must be at or close to NAIRU.	13	1
201506	1388	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	One of the cousins responded that he was not sure who or where “NAIRU” is, but if they’re hiring, they’d certainly look into it.	13	1
201506	1389	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	[Laughter]	13	1
201506	1390	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	All in all, we should be encouraged by the continuing signs of progress in the labor market.	13	1
201506	1391	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	We’re now getting close to the natural rate of unemployment, as defined by participants in the SEP.	13	1
201506	1392	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	When exactly we will reach it is hard to say, because the Committee’s views on the natural rate can change, and because there are some margins of slack remaining that aren’t adequately captured by the difference between U-3 and the estimated natural rate of U-3.	13	1
201506	1393	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	But the unemployment rate is already very close to the natural rate.	13	1
201506	1394	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	As for inflation, I remain reasonably confident that we will see inflation beginning to move back toward our 2 percent target before too long.	13	1
201506	1395	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Core inflation through May was 1.2 percent, a figure that was partly held down by the pass-through of lower oil prices and also by the recent declines in core import prices.	13	1
201506	1396	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	The price of oil now seems to be in a new range, from which it is as likely to move up as to move down.	13	1
201506	1397	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	And the Board staff forecast that core import prices will resume increasing early next year, which will help support core inflation going forward.	13	1
201506	1398	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	As the influence of declining oil, energy, gas prices, and import prices starts to wane, we will begin to see the core inflation rate moving up.	13	1
201506	1399	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	And for the same reason—the relative stabilization of oil prices and the stabilization and possible increase of import prices—we are likely to see total inflation rising as well.	13	1
201506	1400	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	This might not start to happen by September or even this year, but I believe it will happen before long, by which I mean within a year.	13	1
201506	1401	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	And those will be the inflation rates relevant to any changes in monetary policy we put in place in the next few months.	13	1
201506	1402	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I’m reassured that inflation expectations have remained pretty steady, despite the very low levels of headline inflation.	13	1
201506	1403	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	But, overall, it’s not the inflation numbers today that persuade me that we’ll see inflation rising over our projection horizon; rather, it’s my conviction that economic slack has been diminishing and continues to diminish, and that the Phillips curve will reassert itself as the incoming evidence is beginning to suggest.	13	1
201506	1404	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I also put weight on the fact that the SEP results show unanimity on the point that inflation will converge to 2 percent—a unanimity that reflects the view that, over the course of time and—noting what President Kocherlakota said—we can and will attain the target inflation rate.	13	1
201506	1405	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I don’t doubt that the Committee will follow a policy that is aimed at that goal.	13	1
201506	1406	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Now, needless to say, I also have concerns about the outlook.	13	1
201506	1407	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	In particular, consumer spending has been disappointing, particularly when we consider how real incomes have been boosted by lower gasoline prices, and industrial production data have also been disappointing of late.	13	1
201506	1408	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	In addition, we all continue to be aware of the significant downside risks associated with developments in Greece.	13	1
201506	1409	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	On the upside, it’s also possible, of course, that the weakness in the first quarter will prove as transitory as last year’s weakness, and that growth in labor market performance in the remainder of this year could turn out to be more robust than is now forecast.	13	1
