201506	1412	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Tarullo.	13	1
201506	1413	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201506	1414	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Well, obviously, as I think just about everyone has noted, the data over the course of the last couple of weeks has been very encouraging.	13	1
201506	1415	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Stan noted that, at the April meeting, there was a lot of concern.	13	1
201506	1416	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	I think, actually, the concern lasted well into May, so I’m a little more cautious than a lot of people in declaring our uneasiness over, just because it really was the retail sales number and the jobs number— which were, again, undoubtedly good—which turned the tide of some fears that we might be backsliding significantly.	13	1
201506	1417	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Having said that, it is hard to argue, certainly, with the jobs number, and I think there is actually a broader story here, which is that the performance of the labor market has not just been on the unemployment rate side.	13	1
201506	1418	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	As several of you have noted, the slack, which many people saw as not reflected in the unemployment rate over the last few years, did turn out to be there, and it, too, now seems to be contracting somewhat.	13	1
201506	1419	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	I take the fact that the labor participation rate has been flat for the last 18 months as actually very good news, because demographics would suggest that during this period labor participation should have been declining, and, thus, the flatness suggests that people are in fact being pulled back into the labor market.	13	1
201506	1420	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	The question of how much additional slack remains, I still think, is a salient one, and not as easy to answer as the unemployment rate itself might suggest.	13	1
201506	1421	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	So I’m slightly more cautious but join in the general view that we are in a much better position today than we might have thought we would be finding ourselves in just a few weeks ago.	13	1
201506	1422	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Like Vice Chairman Dudley, I also think that what has happened with European sovereigns is basically a good news story.	13	1
201506	1423	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	That is, the extension of negative rates along the yield curve in Europe over the first few months of this year was obviously something that was not sustainable, and potentially its reversal could have been quite destabilizing.	13	1
201506	1424	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	So the fact that those have reversed, particularly the bund yields—in part because of good economic news in Europe and in part, I think, just because people realize that the positions they were taking were not sustainable in any case—is probably a good thing, notwithstanding the fact that it has been accompanied by a modest amount of tightening of financial conditions in the United States.	13	1
201506	1425	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Having said that, first, I can’t come up with a wholly satisfactory explanation of why the reversal went as far as it did.	13	1
201506	1426	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Second, I’m not sure that rates can actually go much further up without negating the benefits of QE in Europe, so we may still have the potential for some dollar strengthening, particularly once we’ve raised rates here.	13	1
201506	1427	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	And, third, if there are significant problems in Greece, I think all bets are off with respect to what happens to sovereign yields throughout Europe, and certainly with regard to a potential spillover effect on the dollar.	13	1
201506	1428	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	The observations about sovereign yields reminds us that a number of questions are lurking just off the path of this prolonged recovery, many of which pertain to the issue of whether developments that predated the crisis have been accelerated or at least become more manifest since then.	13	1
201506	1429	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	In recent work by economists throughout the System, there have been three suggestions along these lines, and I will briefly mention them.	13	1
201506	1430	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	First, President Williams has already alluded to the paper by Rob Valletta and Catherine van der List of the Federal Reserve Bank of San Francisco, who use a cross-state study to find that some portion of the unusually elevated number of workers who are part time for economic reasons may be due to structural factors, such as industry and age composition.	13	1
201506	1431	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Noting that the ratio of PTER to unemployed persons has been rising since 2002, they suggest that some of these factors may be persistent, in which case the part-time-for-economic-reasons ratio may not return all the way to its pre-crisis level.	13	1
201506	1432	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Second, Andrew Figura and David Ratner of the Board staff have looked behind the outward shift in the Beveridge curve and argue that the secular decline in the labor share of income from roughly 70 percent to 63 percent since 2000 has been driven by forces that have also increased the incentives for firms to post more jobs.	13	1
201506	1433	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	So, for example, if diminished worker bargaining power is behind the decline in the labor share, then the return to posting vacancies will be higher for employers.	13	1
201506	1434	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Andrew and David find empirical support for their argument in the fact that industries and states in which the labor share has fallen more have seen higher increases in job postings.	13	1
201506	1435	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	The implication of this research is that even if the long-awaited shift of the Beveridge curve back to its pre-crisis position does not occur, the permanent rightwards movement may not itself reflect an increase in structural unemployment.	13	1
201506	1436	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	And if the curve were eventually to shift back toward its pre-crisis position, the implication would be that the natural rate is even lower than some expect.	13	1
201506	1437	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	On the other hand, if the labor share of income were to reverse its decline while the curve stays shifted to the right, that would imply a higher natural rate, although I should note that Andrew and David place a substantially lesser likelihood on that third outcome than the first two.	13	1
201506	1438	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	The third paper is one by Ekaterina Peneva and Jeremy Rudd of the Board staff that models the relationship of labor cost to price inflation in recent years, finding little evidence that a change in the former has a material effect on the latter.	13	1
201506	1439	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	This is the latest in a line of research that many of us have referred to during these meetings over the last couple of years, suggesting that the past few decades have seen a break in the previous relationship between labor costs and broad price measures.	13	1
201506	1440	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	The authors cast doubt on explanations such as downward nominal wage rigidity for explaining the phenomena that we’ve seen over the past couple of years.	13	1
201506	1441	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Now, not surprisingly, each of these three interesting pieces of research leaves some questions unanswered.	13	1
201506	1442	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	The work on PTER focuses on a pretty short and, in macroeconomic terms, pretty unusual time period.	13	1
201506	1443	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	In addition, some of the factors identified by the authors as structural, such as industry and age composition, tend themselves to move with the business cycle, so it may be a little bit difficult to disentangle what is structural from what is cyclical.	13	1
201506	1444	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	The Figura-Ratner work does not directly measure the loss of bargaining power, but instead shows the relationship that’s theoretically consistent with such a shift.	13	1
201506	1445	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	And, of course, the Peneva–Rudd paper itself notes that its undermining of labor costs as a key explanatory factor driving inflation leaves unanswered the question of the most important dynamics that are determining price inflation today.	13	1
201506	1446	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	But these three recent lines of research are yet another reminder that relationships observed and established in the pre-crisis period may actually have been changing in ways that the Great Recession has made more palpable.	13	1
201506	1447	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	And I mention them today not simply to advertise the interesting work being done around the System, although that’s probably a worthwhile thing to do, but also because I think they’re trying to help inform the monetary policy decisions that we’re going to have to make over the next several meetings.	13	1
201506	1448	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	In particular, the Peneva-Rudd paper, adding itself to that line of research to which I alluded earlier, does for me, at least, put into sharp relief the question of when one can be reasonably confident that inflation will return to the 2 percent target.	13	1
201506	1449	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201506	1450	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1

201506	1453	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	I will begin, as others have, with the questions that hung in the air at the time of the April meeting.	13	1
201506	1454	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Specifically, was the first quarter really as bad as it seemed?	13	1
201506	1455	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	And, second, how much signal should we take for the path forward?	13	1
201506	1456	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	I would agree with many voices around the table that incoming data since the April meeting tentatively offer encouraging answers on both questions.	13	1
201506	1457	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	The discussion in Tealbook, Book A, on special factors in the first quarter, which I found very useful and thoughtful, suggests that underlying growth was in the range of 1 percent in the first quarter.	13	1
201506	1458	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Some other outside estimates see an even greater one-time effect and, thus, stronger underlying growth.	13	1
201506	1459	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	So I’m inclined to believe that there was no sharp break in the pace of underlying growth in Q1, especially with real GDI growing at 1.4 percent and monthly payroll gains of nearly 200,000.	13	1
201506	1460	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	As for the second quarter and the rest of the year, incoming data have picked up since the April meeting, particularly in those areas in which there had been the worrisome weakness.	13	1
201506	1461	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	The April and May employment reports showed job gains reaccelerating after a lull in March.	13	1
201506	1462	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	The May retail sales estimate also struck a significantly more positive note, with solid growth for May and upward revisions for March and April.	13	1
201506	1463	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	And since growth is so heavily dependent on the consumer at the moment, that news was particularly important.	13	1
201506	1464	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	The Michigan survey also provided more support for that positive spending narrative, with a significant uptick in confidence and the highest ratings for personal financial prospects and wage expectations since before the crisis.	13	1
201506	1465	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	I also found the staff memo that Glenn Follette had taken part in writing to be striking a generally positive note on labor market conditions as well.	13	1
201506	1466	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Housing starts have also strengthened, and although I don’t expect a lot out of this sector in terms of being a major engine of growth, a small positive contribution is welcome.	13	1
201506	1467	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Turning to my SEP submission, I have marked down a slightly stronger growth rate for real GDP this year than is shown in the Tealbook and about the same as the Tealbook thereafter.	13	1
201506	1468	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	On the unemployment front, I also believe that there is a significant chance that unemployment will drop faster and further than in the baseline forecast, given the payroll and productivity forecasts.	13	1
201506	1469	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Compared with the relationship we’ve seen over the course of the last couple of years, the Tealbook forecast calls for unemployment to drop significantly more slowly for a given amount of payroll growth for reasons—perfectly possible reasons—that I’ve spent many happy hours discussing with the staff, but I guess I’ll just go for now with what’s been happening for the last couple of years.	13	1
201506	1470	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	By putting a little more weight on the recent trend, I’ve got unemployment declining to around 5 percent by the end of this year and dipping below 5 percent in 2016 and 2017.	13	1
201506	1471	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	With the economy slightly tighter, I’ve got inflation getting to 2 percent by 2017.	13	1
201506	1472	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	More on that tomorrow.	13	1
201506	1473	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	These changes do happen to bring my forecast into closer alignment with the run of public forecasts I’ve seen, as I think was implicit in Glenn’s earlier presentation.	13	1
201506	1474	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Market expectations for the path of policy rates have moved up significantly since the April meeting, and appropriately so.	13	1
201506	1475	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Although Treasury rates have run up recently, we’ve seen similar or larger moves often over the last 30 years, even in the good old days before the post- crisis decline in liquidity.	13	1
201506	1476	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Although volatility in the Treasury securities market has increased in recent months, that leaves the MOVE index, which measures volatility in fixed income markets across the curve, closer to but still below typical volatility levels for the decade before the financial crisis.	13	1
201506	1477	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	And I guess the best way to make sure that we don’t trigger undue increases in volatility is to continue to avoid surprising the markets unnecessarily.	13	1
201506	1478	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	In any event, both short- and long-term rates now seem to me to be better aligned with economic fundamentals than they have been, and that gives me some cause for hope—optimism that we can avoid an episode of harmful volatility.	13	1
201506	1479	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	There’s also been much greater volatility in the euro area, particularly in German fixed income markets recently, but this seems to me to relate principally to some correction after the strong initial reaction to the ECB’s quantitative easing program.	13	1
201506	1480	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	And I would echo Governor Tarullo’s and Vice Chairman Dudley’s comments, at least that I don’t take any negative signal for our normalization process—those are my words—from what happened in Europe during the intermeeting period.	13	1
201506	1481	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	I will close with the observation that the Tealbook baseline and my SEP submission are based on the assumption that no important fallout arises from the ongoing Greek crisis.	13	1
201506	1482	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	The range of possible outcomes is wide—and of possible implications is even wider.	13	1

201506	1489	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Madam Chair, the mixed data since we met in April haven’t fully resolved questions about the economy’s underlying momentum.	13	1
201506	1490	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	While it’s clear that some portion of the weakness in the first quarter resulted from a combination of transitory factors— residual seasonality, bad weather, and the port strike—it also appears likely that the economy’s underlying momentum may have softened because of somewhat persistent effects from exchange rates, oil prices, and cautious consumers.	13	1
201506	1491	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	While the data in hand pertaining to the second quarter are mostly reassuring, they don’t suggest a sufficient bounceback to compensate for the first- quarter weakness and certainly are not as strong as what we saw this time last year.	13	1
201506	1492	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Even after incorporating the positive first-quarter Quarterly Services Survey and the May retail sales and housing permits data, it now looks as though real GDP will advance at a disappointing 1¼ percent annual rate over the first half of the year.	13	1
201506	1493	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The most likely explanation for the persistent component of this weakness is that the negative effects of the recent rise in the exchange rate and the reduction in oil prices on net exports and business investment have been larger than expected, likely subtracting around 1½ percentage points from growth over the first half of the year, while the positive effects, which should be reflected primarily in consumer spending, have not materialized as projected.	13	1
201506	1494	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The lackluster pace of household spending is surprising, in view of the variety of factors present that would normally be supportive.	13	1
201506	1495	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Real interest rates remain quite low by historical standards.	13	1
201506	1496	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Housing wealth and equity wealth have each increased at double-digit rates on average over the past two years.	13	1
201506	1497	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Robust job gains and falling energy prices have contributed to increases in real incomes of 3½ percent over the past year.	13	1
201506	1498	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	And households appear to understand these favorable conditions, as consumer sentiment is at relatively elevated levels.	13	1
201506	1499	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	And yet reported real consumer spending likely increased only a little over 2 percent in the first quarter, and even the four-quarter increase of around 3 percent is short of what the fundamental determinants of spending and historical correlations would suggest.	13	1
201506	1500	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Spending on new homes has also been disappointing, and starts remain far below the trend increases consistent with population growth, although the May data on single-family permits was a bright spot.	13	1
201506	1501	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	It’s at least possible that household behavior continues to be shaped by the experience of the financial crisis and the Great Recession, with an increased perception of tail risks and concerns among many consumers that increases in income and wealth may be highly contingent and subject to reversal.	13	1
201506	1502	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	If, as a result, households are reluctant to spend out of any gains, the headwinds holding back aggregate demand may prove somewhat persistent.	13	1
201506	1503	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Developments abroad are another source of potential ongoing headwinds.	13	1
201506	1504	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Slow growth in aggregate demand abroad and its effects on the exchange rate of the dollar continue to weigh on goods production in the United States.	13	1
201506	1505	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	We learned earlier this week that manufacturing production declined in May.	13	1
201506	1506	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	That will be a reduction in manufacturing output of over 1 percent at an annual rate over the past six months after increasing at close to 5 percent in the preceding 12 months; staff models predict that recent increases in the value of the dollar will remain a significant drag on net exports for some time to come.	13	1
201506	1507	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	That projection is based on a relatively stable dollar and a pickup in foreign growth, but the risk of a messy Greek exit from the euro zone has increased of late, as has the risk of persistent weakness in aggregate demand abroad.	13	1
201506	1508	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Most immediately, negotiations between official creditors and the Greek government are at a very delicate stage, and it’s not clear a compromise solution is attainable.	13	1
201506	1509	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	At the same time, incoming data on foreign GDP growth were once again weaker than expected, with China’s growth outlook murky, and commodity producers negatively affected.	13	1
201506	1510	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Despite this, our labor market continues to improve.	13	1
201506	1511	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	May’s employment report offers a welcome reassurance on this front.	13	1
201506	1512	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Employment gains have averaged close to 220,000 in 2015, down from the pace of 2014, but as many have noted, still at a very respectable pace.	13	1
201506	1513	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The unemployment rate, which had fallen at close to one-tenth of a percentage point per month over 2013 and 2014, has declined only one-tenth percentage point over the past five months, but it appears that resource slack continues to diminish, now concentrated in other margins such as the participation rate, which is very welcome.	13	1
201506	1514	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Although aggregate measures of wage growth remain relatively low, on balance, here too we’re seeing signs of acceleration.	13	1
201506	1515	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Both the 12-month changes in the employment cost index and average hourly earnings have moved up recently, and other indicators also point upward.	13	1
201506	1516	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	These are, of course, very welcome indications, but I’ll want to see sustained momentum to be convinced this represents a broad-based, convincing step-up in wage growth.	13	1
201506	1517	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The change in average hourly earnings is not yet meaningfully different from the 2 percent average pace of the past several years, and the staff’s current estimate of the four-quarter change in the other main gauge of wage growth, business-sector compensation per hour, is only 1¾ percent in the first quarter.	13	1
201506	1518	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The continued disconnect between very robust improvement in the labor market and disappointing overall economic growth raises questions about why productivity growth has been so miserable and the extent to which this reflects headwinds from the crisis, which may be reversed, or some more sustained structural change.	13	1
201506	1519	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	This issue is so central to our assessment of the output gap, resource slack, and appropriate policy that it’s important to get a better understanding of it in our analysis as we go forward.	13	1
201506	1520	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Finally, turning to inflation, core PCE inflation has increased from the low monthly rate seen around the turn of the year, with the annualized three-month change in prices at around 1½ percent in May compared with ½ percent in January.	13	1
201506	1521	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Consumer energy prices seem likely to increase at a double-digit annualized rate this quarter and boost a change in total PCE prices to close to 2 percent.	13	1
201506	1522	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	But the support to inflation from energy price increases will also be transitory, and measures of the underlying pace of price increases, such as the 12-month change in core PCE prices or the Federal Reserve Bank of Dallas’ 12-month trimmed mean rate, are still noticeably below our 2 percent target.	13	1
201506	1523	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	So while the downside risks to the inflation outlook have diminished, there’s still no sign of core inflation moving above the 1½ percent pace it has remained near over the course of the recovery.	13	1
201506	1524	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	So, overall, the slowing in the pace of the economic improvement since the beginning of the year is difficult for me to dismiss entirely as an anomaly based on the data we have to date.	13	1
201506	1525	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	It’s therefore of substantial value to gather more information about the underlying momentum in economic activity in the coming months before we take action.	13	1

201506	1567	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	On the business spending side, indicators of business sentiment have been less reassuring and business investment has been somewhat disappointing, with drilling activity continuing to contract sharply and orders and shipments of capital goods staying flat.	13	1

201506	1569	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	The softness in business spending has been offset to some extent of late by a stronger-than-expected pickup in residential investment, and recent data have been somewhat encouraging with respect to housing.	13	1
201506	1570	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	We did have some discussion of the implications of the recent weakness in labor productivity, which, as of the first quarter, had risen only ¼ percent on a year-over-year basis.	13	1
201506	1571	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Many of you noted this is going to be a very important factor in determining how the labor market performs in the period ahead.	13	1
201506	1572	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	If this poor performance continues, we may see continued substantial improvement in labor market conditions and upward pressure on inflation even if real GDP growth remains tepid.	13	1
201506	1573	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	But if, as the staff is projecting, productivity growth was to return to a more normal level, we would need to see and be confident that we have a meaningful pickup in output growth just to stabilize the unemployment rate near its current level.	13	1
201506	1574	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Finally, many of you mentioned continued risks coming from abroad, obviously including the still-unsettled Greek debt situation and the possibility that a disorderly outcome could have adverse consequences for us through exchange rate effects and other channels.	13	1
201506	1575	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	And a number of you noted risks stemming from China and growth in emerging markets.	13	1
201506	1576	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	On the inflation front, incoming data came in pretty close to staff expectations.	13	1
201506	1577	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Very few of you noted any significant change in your outlook.	13	1
201506	1578	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Total PCE inflation was only 0.1 percent over the last year.	13	1
201506	1579	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Core PCE prices, which is, I think, a better indicator of the underlying trend, rose only 1.2 percent.	13	1
201506	1580	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	These were largely in line with Tealbook predictions.	13	1
201506	1581	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	However, many of you noted that crude oil prices have stabilized, and the real exchange rate is stable or up only slightly since the last FOMC meeting.	13	1
201506	1582	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	And while there will be a very long lag between the stabilization in oil prices and an upward move in headline inflation, we are not likely to see a big upward movement until close to the end of the year.	13	1
201506	1583	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Eventually, the downward pressure of those huge declines in energy prices near the end of the year will drop out, and headline inflation will move up toward core.	13	1
201506	1584	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	A number of you noted that the appreciation of the dollar is depressing import prices, and our staff estimates that that’s taking probably ¼ percentage point off core inflation this year.	13	1
201506	1585	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	With respect to the likely behavior of core inflation in the period ahead, the staff estimate that for the rest of the year it should be running close to 1½ percent, and your updated SEP projections look like they are consistent with that assessment.	13	1
201506	1586	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	So when we turn to the critical issue of whether recent developments have made you reasonably confident or increased your confidence that the level of inflation will actually move up to 2 percent over the next couple of years, a number of you noted that the fact that the dollar and oil prices have stabilized does raise your confidence that headline inflation will move up toward core.	13	1
201506	1587	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	An important question, however, with core inflation still running below 2 percent, is, what will happen to that core rate over time?	13	1
201506	1588	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	A number of you indicated that as long as the labor market continues to improve, you have confidence that the Phillips curve will assert itself.	13	1
201506	1589	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	And with stable inflation expectations, inflation will tend to move up toward 2 percent over time, although we have to be sure that growth is strong enough to get that outcome.	13	1
201506	1590	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	But several of you expressed deeper concerns about whether or not that’s a reasonable prediction.	13	1
201506	1591	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans emphasized the fact that there’s some evidence in the Survey of Professional Forecasters that CPI inflation expectations have drifted down.	13	1
201506	1592	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Kocherlakota expressed concern about whether inflation will move up, whether our inflation target is credible, given the Committee’s apparent lack of determination to move inflation up over time, and he also noted that it looks as though the risks around a 2 percent medium-term inflation forecast may not be symmetric—they may be weighted to the downside.	13	1
201506	1593	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	So let me stop there with those comments.	13	1

201506	1595	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	[No response]	13	1
201506	1596	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Okay, then let me add a couple of comments of my own, and they’ll be directed toward what we have learned and what we haven’t learned since our previous meeting.	13	1
201506	1597	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Back in April, we faced a wide range of surprisingly weak readings on the labor market and real activity more broadly.	13	1
201506	1598	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	We thought this softness was largely transitory, but we couldn’t be sure it wasn’t the beginning of a more serious stalling of the expansion.	13	1
201506	1599	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	And now, it seems to me, that with payroll gains running close to 210,000 in the past three months and real GDP now apparently expanding at least at a moderate pace, that we were experiencing a temporary pause in activity.	13	1
201506	1600	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	That said, the Tealbook estimates that real GDP is going to expand at only a pretty paltry 1¼ percent annual rate in the first half of the year, even with a decent rebound in activity in the current quarter.	13	1
201506	1601	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	And the tone of some key monthly indicators has remained persistently soft.	13	1
201506	1602	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	So it’s unclear whether real GDP over the rest of the year will be strong enough to sustain further improvement in the labor market, even with the funds rate near zero.	13	1
201506	1603	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	We can’t expect any support from net exports this year, in view of the weak state of the global economy and elevated level of the dollar.	13	1
201506	1604	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Indeed, the potential for things to worsen on this front is, in my view, material.	13	1
201506	1605	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	For example, a disorderly resolution of the Greek situation could put further upward pressure on the dollar.	13	1
201506	1606	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	We can’t expect much support from government spending, in light of fiscal realities at the federal, state, and local levels.	13	1
201506	1607	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Residential investment isn’t likely to be a significant source of strength either, even with the recent uptick in permits and starts.	13	1
201506	1608	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	In part, this is simply because housing is such a small share of GDP.	13	1
201506	1609	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	But beyond that, I think it’s unlikely, as long as credit availability remains so tight, that housing construction will contribute a lot to real GDP growth anytime soon.	13	1
201506	1610	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	I mentioned that business fixed investment has been weaker—at least weaker than I expected so far.	13	1
201506	1611	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	I know a lot of it reflects the contraction in drilling, which should be temporary, especially now that oil prices have flattened out.	13	1
201506	1612	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	But the softness extends beyond this category.	13	1
201506	1613	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Maybe it is expected—and I think it is in line with staff expectations—that firms would be reluctant to engage in much capital spending in an environment of only slow growth and aggregate demand, both at home and abroad.	13	1
201506	1614	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	But, at any rate, business surveys do point to only moderate investment growth, at best, in coming months, and that leaves consumer spending.	13	1
201506	1615	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	While household spending now looks to have expanded at a solid pace during the first half of the year, growth, nonetheless, has slowed noticeably since the second half of last year.	13	1
201506	1616	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	And, as I mentioned, that occurred despite the very large boost to real income from lower energy prices.	13	1
201506	1617	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	It raises the possibility that we may have overestimated the stimulus from this windfall, both to date and over the rest of the year.	13	1
201506	1618	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	The Tealbook projects real PCE growth to pick up to 3½ percent in the second half of this year.	13	1
201506	1619	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	It also projects that the saving rate will decline appreciably.	13	1
201506	1620	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	But if the saving rate were to instead move just sideways through the end of the year, then real GDP would likely increase only 1 percent or so for the year as a whole.	13	1
201506	1621	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, even mediocre GDP growth would not necessarily be inconsistent with further improvement in labor market conditions if the pace of productivity gains remains very low.	13	1
201506	1622	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	If that were to occur, we could see employment continuing to rise steadily and the unemployment rate falling to 5 percent relatively soon.	13	1
201506	1623	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Depending on the accompanying inflation data, such an outcome would likely warrant increasing the federal funds rate even though overall economic activity was expanding quite slowly.	13	1
201506	1624	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	But a development of that type would also imply that the economy’s equilibrium real interest rate is lower than we now estimate, suggesting both the need to tighten policy less in the longer run and also a greater risk of returning to the zero lower bound—in short, a more gradual trajectory for interest rates.	13	1
201506	1625	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	On the inflation front, incoming information has similarly clarified some issues and left others unresolved.	13	1
201506	1626	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	On the positive side, the data have come in more or less as expected, and I think they convincingly demonstrate that the current very low readings on inflation are substantially the result of transitory factors—namely, oil prices and the dollar.	13	1
201506	1627	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	So I feel reasonably confident that by early next year, PCE inflation on a 12-month basis will be back to the neighborhood of 1½ percent, assuming that energy prices and the dollar do remain roughly stable.	13	1
201506	1628	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	On the other hand, I’m uncertain whether inflation will continue climbing after that point and reach our inflation objective within two to three years.	13	1
201506	1629	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	For me to be reasonably confident on this score, I’d have to see both further improvement in the labor market and evidence that GDP growth is likely to stay sufficiently strong to complete the return to full employment even as interest rates rise.	13	1
201506	1630	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	I suppose I’m in the camp that’s prepared to believe in the Phillips curve, but it’s going to take, in my mind, confidence the labor market will improve.	13	1
201506	1631	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	And without that assurance, I would worry that resource utilization might not prove to be persistently tight enough to bring inflation back to 2 percent over the medium term, even if inflation expectations remain well anchored.	13	1
201506	1632	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	To anticipate our policy discussion, I think we need more information before we can confidently say that conditions warrant raising the federal funds rate.	13	1
201506	1633	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	It’s unrealistic to expect that all doubts will be erased by our September meeting, but at that point we will have received six labor reports since we first stated the conditions necessary to initiate tightening, and that’s a solid basis for assessing whether labor market conditions have improved sufficiently to initiate tightening.	13	1
201506	1634	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	As the year progresses, we’ll also get additional readings on real activity and productivity, and I think we’ll be in a better position to judge the likelihood that growth will stay strong enough to keep the economy moving back to full employment, and, thus, for us to be reasonably confident that inflation will gradually move back to 2 percent.	13	1

201506	1638	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Thank you, Madam Chair.	21	2
201506	1639	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	I didn’t quite muster the courage to break decisively with dress code in this room, but in appreciation of President Williams’s gift that I have here with me, I managed to slip seven mentions of “data dependence” or “data dependent” into my text.	21	2
201506	1640	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	I will be referring to the handout labeled “Material for Briefing on Monetary Policy Alternatives.”	21	2
201506	1641	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	At the April meeting, the Committee decided that economic conditions had progressed to the point that the decision to begin normalizing policy could be taken at any meeting, starting with the current one.	21	2
201506	1642	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Therefore, we thought it appropriate that the alternatives include a draft postmeeting statement that announces the beginning of policy normalization and a note that communicates related operational decisions.	21	2
201506	1643	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	I will return to those later in my briefing.	21	2
201506	1644	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Under the assumption that the Committee will not choose to raise the target range for the federal funds rate at this meeting, the key issue, taking as given your principle of data dependence, is how to characterize the economic outlook and related risks.	21	2
201506	1645	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The remaining three alternatives approach this issue in various ways.	21	2
201506	1646	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Before turning to these alternatives, my first exhibit reviews some evidence regarding whether market participants understand that the Committee is now on a meeting-by-meeting basis regarding the timing of liftoff, and that its decisions are data dependent.	21	2
201506	1647	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	I focus on three questions:  whether uncertainty about the economic outlook is reflected in an appropriate degree of uncertainty about the timing of the first tightening, whether interest rates are correspondingly sensitive to incoming economic information and its implications for the outlook, and whether investors appear to appreciate the data dependence of the pace of tightening beyond your first move.	21	2
201506	1648	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The upper-right panel shows the average of primary dealers’ probability distributions regarding the meeting at which you will first raise the target range of the federal funds rate.	21	2
201506	1649	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As Simon noted, while the highest probability is on September, roughly equal probability is attached to liftoff at a later date.	21	2
201506	1650	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The probabilities are spread out across future meetings, as they ought to be in light of your message of data dependence and the inherent uncertainty of future economic developments.	21	2
201506	1651	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The middle-left panel shows that quotes on federal funds futures also imply a risk-neutral probability distribution that is consistent with data dependence.	21	2
201506	1652	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Both panels indicate that, since your April meeting, the odds of liftoff at the September meeting have increased, partly reflecting the reduced probability placed on liftoff at the current meeting in the wake of the string of soft spending data.	21	2
201506	1653	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The odds of liftoff after September are little changed, on balance, consistent with your assessment that economic weakness in the first quarter will prove to be transitory.	21	2
201506	1654	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The middle-right panel provides some evidence regarding the second question, whether interest rates are as sensitive to incoming economic news as one should expect.	21	2
201506	1655	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The panel shows indexes for the response of the 2-year and 10-year Treasury yields to macroeconomic news, where the shaded region shows the period since the federal funds rate reached the lower bound.	21	2
201506	1656	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As shown by the red line, from 2010 until the end of 2012, the sensitivity of the 2-year yield fell to almost zero as markets—correctly—anticipated that short-term rates would remain at the lower bound for at least a few years.	21	2
201506	1657	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Since then, the sensitivity has retraced much of this decline and is now closer to normal levels, as economic news now has a meaningful effect on expectations of short-term rates over the next two years.	21	2
201506	1658	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The sensitivity of the 10-year yield, by contrast, has declined from its recent peak during the taper tantrum and is now at a historically normal level.	21	2
201506	1659	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Sadly, from a macroeconomist’s perspective, macroeconomic news explains only a small fraction of overall interest rate variations.	21	2
201506	1660	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The lower-left panel shows that, more generally, uncertainty about the level of short-term interest rates one year ahead has followed a broadly similar path to the red line in the middle right, and since early 2014 it has begun to move back toward more normal levels, although it still has some way to go.	21	2
201506	1661	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The fact that uncertainty about the federal funds rate one year hence remains well below historical norms could, in turn, reflect the strength of market participants’ conviction of a very gradual pace of tightening once it begins.	21	2
201506	1662	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The panel in the lower-right shows the average probability distribution across primary dealers of the federal funds rate target increases during the first year of tightening, conditional on the federal funds rate target not returning to its current range.	21	2
201506	1663	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	These probabilities are tightly clustered around roughly 100 basis points per year, with only negligible odds on economic scenarios under which the Committee would tighten at a pace faster than what was considered “measured” in the mid-2000s, indicated by the vertical line.	21	2
201506	1664	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	It is not clear whether the high probability mass around roughly 100 basis points per year reflects a high degree of confidence that economic conditions will evolve in a manner consistent with this gradual pace, or whether it represents a lack of appreciation of the data dependence of future monetary policy.	21	2
201506	1665	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Summing up, the evidence presented on this exhibit suggests that there is a healthy dispersion of probabilities over when the economic conditions for the first tightening will have been met, and financial market prices seem reasonably responsive to economic news.	21	2
201506	1666	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Yet, financial markets may still throw a “liftoff tantrum,” either because they come to anticipate a greater likelihood of a historically more-normal pace of tightening, or because the data I am reviewing are unreliable guides to market expectations.	21	2
201506	1667	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Turning to your consideration of today’s decision and the postmeeting statement, the bullet points at the top of the second exhibit outline how the draft language in alternatives A, B, and C address the range of possible assessments that the Committee might make about economic developments over the intermeeting period and their implications for progress toward the Committee’s criteria for beginning normalization.	21	2
201506	1668	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Alternative B would indicate that the economy is expanding moderately and would continue to characterize the labor market in terms of the pace at which underutilization is diminishing.	21	2
201506	1669	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Although the Committee would acknowledge that inflation is still running below 2 percent, it would temper that observation by noting that “earlier declines in energy prices” have been a factor in holding down inflation and report that “energy prices appear to have stabilized.”	21	2
201506	1670	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The assessment of the outlook in paragraph 2 of alternative B is basically unchanged:  The Committee continues to anticipate that, with appropriate policy accommodation, the economy will expand moderately, leading to further progress toward the Committee’s goals.	21	2
201506	1671	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	And alternative B would repeat the guidance in paragraph 3.	21	2
201506	1672	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	All told, the draft language in alternative B would communicate that some progress has been made since the last meeting on both of the Committee’s criteria for policy firming, but that the Committee, while expecting further progress, remains data dependent and will decide on the stance of policy on a meeting-by-meeting basis.	21	2
201506	1673	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	By retaining all future meetings as live options, alternative B would allow for the possibility that policy firming could begin in July or September.	21	2
201506	1674	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	At the same time, it would also leave open the possibility that data on the economy might evolve in a way that would warrant a later start.	21	2
201506	1675	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	While alternative B would not tip your hand regarding the likely timing of when the conditions for liftoff will have been met, alternatives C or A would send such a signal.	21	2
201506	1676	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	With the language in alternative C, the Committee would convey the view that it has seen appreciable progress toward meeting its criteria for beginning policy normalization and thus it would likely be read by the public as suggesting that the first increase in the target federal funds rate is close.	21	2
201506	1677	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In contrast to alternative B, paragraphs 1 and 2 of alternative C would use language more closely tied to the Committee’s stated criteria for increasing the target range for the federal funds rate.	21	2
201506	1678	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In paragraph 1, the Committee would indicate that it has seen “some improvement in labor market conditions,” and by omitting the reference to underutilization of labor resources, might leave the impression that such underutilization has mostly vanished.	21	2
201506	1679	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In addition, paragraph 2 would express greater confidence in the outlook for inflation, indicating that “the risk of inflation running persistently below 2 percent has diminished.”	21	2
201506	1680	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The views on economic activity and the outlook in alternative A would instead suggest that the Committee has seen little further progress toward meeting the criteria for the start of policy firming and would likely push out market expectations for policy tightening into the tail of the current distribution.	21	2
201506	1681	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Paragraph 2 would indicate that the risks to the outlook for economic activity, the labor market, and inflation are all to the downside.	21	2
201506	1682	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The concern about inflation would be sufficiently strong that the Committee would strengthen the criteria for policy normalization, stating in paragraphs 3 and 4 that inflation would need to be anticipated to reach 2 percent within one to two years and that the Committee is prepared to use all its tools to meet that criterion.	21	2
201506	1683	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As I noted at the beginning of my briefing, I want to conclude with some remarks on alternative C′ and on the staff proposal for communicating details of the Committee’s operational approach to implementing policy when policy firming commences.	21	2
201506	1684	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	We would very much appreciate your comments on these during the Q&A period and the policy go-round.	21	2
201506	1685	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	As highlighted in the first set of bullet points at the bottom of the page, the most significant change that you will need to make to a postmeeting statement announcing the initial increase in the target range for the federal funds rate will be to update the forward guidance about how the Committee will approach subsequent adjustments in the target range.	21	2
201506	1686	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Following from the existing forward guidance, the proposed language in paragraph 3 of alternative C′ would, first, reiterate that the Committee’s decisions will be made in response to economic and financial developments and their implications for the economic outlook, so as to promote the mandated objectives.	21	2
201506	1687	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In line with your current SEP responses, the draft language in C′ would explicitly note that the Committee expects that the economic outlook will warrant a gradual increase, and would retain the assessment that even after employment and inflation are near mandate-consistent levels, economic conditions may, for some time, warrant keeping the target federal funds rate below longer-run normal levels.	21	2
201506	1688	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	However, in order to communicate that the Committee’s assessment of the appropriate path for the federal funds rate might change as economic conditions evolve, the proposed language adds that adjustments to the target range will be data driven.	21	2
201506	1689	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The final set of bullet points focuses on the staff’s proposal that the postmeeting statement be accompanied by a document providing the operational details associated with a change in the federal funds rate target.	21	2
201506	1690	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Rather than repeat the details covered in the memo that you received last week, I will just briefly highlight what we see as the advantages of this approach.	21	2
201506	1691	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	The Committee’s previous communications regarding policy normalization have indicated that adjustments to the target range for the federal funds rate will remain its primary means of conveying the stance of monetary policy, and that the Board’s adjustments to the IOER rate and the Committee’s instructions to the Desk regarding the operation of the ON RRP facility—and possibly other tools—are intended to be used to help maintain the federal funds rate within the target range.	21	2
201506	1692	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	We propose that the Committee’s postmeeting statement focus clearly and simply on your decision about the stance of policy and the reasons for that decision, while avoiding the possible distractions that could arise from including additional information on the use of, and possible adjustments to, supporting operational tools.	21	2
201506	1693	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	A separate document concerning implementation details may prove to be particularly useful in the event that the Committee needs to make an intermeeting adjustment to the operational tools after the commencement of policy firming to keep the federal funds rate in an unchanged target range.	21	2
201506	1694	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In addition, the document on policy implementation would consolidate information about the use of these tools without highlighting their differences in governance.	21	2
201506	1695	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Copies of all four draft alternatives and their associated policy directives are attached to my exhibits.	21	2
201506	1696	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Note that the draft directive for alternative C′ incorporates the changes that were discussed in the June 10 memo, while the draft directive for the other alternatives offers the option of making several changes proposed in the same memo that are intended as “housekeeping” items to bring the directive up-to-date.	21	2
201506	1697	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	If you will turn to page 14 of your packet, you will see that the first change is to eliminate the reference to managing conditions in reserve markets—which is not how you are now conducting policy—and add the specific reference to the federal funds rate target range.	21	2
201506	1698	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In the second paragraph, the rewording of the first sentence avoids the possible misinterpretation that “its policy” refers to the Desk’s rather than the Committee’s.	21	2
201506	1699	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	And, finally, the last sentence, which was added in December 2008 when emergency lending and the first LSAP were having substantial effects on the balance sheet, seems no longer necessary.	21	2
201506	1700	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	In particular, the Rules of Organization dictate that the SOMA manager is responsible for keeping the Committee informed about market conditions and transactions made for the SOMA, and these reports have become a regular feature of each meeting.	21	2

201506	1707	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Well, I just have a question on the tradeoff between data dependence and forward guidance.	22	2
201506	1708	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	When I look at the probability that you have in your top- right panel in exhibit 1, we have a roughly 45 percent probability of moving in September, and presumably, if the data comes in as forecast, that probability would improve on its own as we get into July.	22	2
201506	1709	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I guess the goal would be to get that much closer to 80 or 90 percent, since we wouldn’t be comfortable that 45 or 55 was quite enough.	22	2
201506	1710	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	And I just want to think about what the relative benefit of getting that additional increase would be as we get into September, particularly if the data surprises us in August and we end up having to backtrack.	22	2
201506	1711	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	So we’ve moved into an environment in which we’ve tried to avoid forward guidance, and we’ve really highlighted data dependence in speeches and in what we’ve put into the statement.	22	2
201506	1712	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Can you give me the relative cost and benefit of adding in language that moves away from data dependence—to tip our hat a little bit more—and how much additional benefit we would get from tipping our hat versus what happens if we tip our hat and turn out to be wrong?	22	2
201506	1713	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	So I don’t have a clear view on what should be some kind of target value for this probability.	22	2
201506	1714	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	Would it be ideal if, in fact, market expectations were close to 100 percent right before the meeting?	22	2
201506	1715	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	It would seem to me that probably there is going to be some residual uncertainty simply because your assessment of economic conditions and whether they warrant liftoff or not always will involve a certain amount of judgment—that is very difficult to boil down to a simple formula.	22	2
201506	1716	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	So my sense is that you wouldn’t want to raise that probability too high, in that you would want to avoid leaving the impression that expectations are being completely piled up on liftoff at a particular meeting—that would be a serious impediment.	22	2
201506	1717	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	My thinking here is more that market participants should simply be sufficiently attuned to the fact that you may judge the data as being consistent with liftoff being warranted at that meeting, so that it is not being perceived as a breakdown in communications.	22	2
201506	1718	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	More generally speaking, my sense is that there was a time when forward guidance could be used in a fairly hard data-dependent sense, like we did with your threshold strategy, in which you could make firm commitments that before 6½ was crossed, the conversation would not even begin.	22	2
201506	1719	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	At this point, however, when you are so close to these criteria, I think it is just very difficult to lay out very precise, specific guidance of exactly which economic conditions we will see as warranting liftoff ex ante.	22	2
201506	1720	2015-06-17	meeting	LAUBACH	I’m afraid I’m not giving you a very precise answer, but I think that probabilities in this range or higher should be fine.	22	2
201506	1721	2015-06-17	meeting	POTTER	I could give some history, just quickly.	22	2
201506	1722	2015-06-17	meeting	POTTER	If we look back to September 2013, the probability of a taper, on average, was around 50 percent.	22	2
201506	1723	2015-06-17	meeting	POTTER	And at the time, most people thought that the Fed would taper, there was a pretty wide range of views there, and that was about that actual meeting.	22	2
201506	1724	2015-06-17	meeting	POTTER	I think if the average was 70 percent—and the history shows that it doesn’t really get much higher than that unless there’s been a direct telegraphing that it’s going to happen—if there’s still a big wide range of views, so some people are still at 30 and some are at 90 or something, then that’s not a great situation to be in because we don’t know who the marginal investor is.	22	2
201506	1725	2015-06-17	meeting	POTTER	Is the marginal investor the one at 30 percent or the one at 90 percent?	22	2

201506	1984	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201506	1985	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	I support option B.	23	2
201506	1986	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	We certainly would not want our first tightening of monetary policy from the zero lower bound to coincide with the default of a developed country.	23	2
201506	1987	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Because of the uncertainties abroad, this would not have been the appropriate time for the first tightening, even if the domestic conditions we had set out initially had been met.	23	2
201506	1988	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, in my view, both conditions have yet to be met.	23	2
201506	1989	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Core PCE over the past year, at 1.2 percent, has been falling, not rising, and the U-3 unemployment rate has leveled off rather than continuing to improve.	23	2
201506	1990	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In a low-inflation environment at the zero lower bound, it is instructive that the most common mistakes made by major central banks to date have been premature tightenings.	23	2
201506	1991	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Japan had a liftoff of rates in August 2000 and again in July 2006, yet both were subsequently reversed, and even today Japan remains far from its inflation goal.	23	2
201506	1992	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	Similarly, the ECB tightened in April 2011 before reversing course only seven months later, and Sweden raised rates in July 2010 only to reverse course.	23	2
201506	1993	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	None of the central banks that raised rates and then reversed have hit their inflation targets recently.	23	2
201506	1994	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	To say the least, their reversals of policy and their subsequent inability to hit their inflation targets have not been confidence-building exercises.	23	2
201506	1995	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The inherent asymmetry in our ability to offset shocks when at the zero lower bound is something to be taken very seriously.	23	2
201506	1996	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	We have a limited ability to offset unexpected weakness but a nearly limitless ability to offset unexpected strength.	23	2
201506	1997	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	We should learn from the mistakes of other central banks and tighten only when we are clearly on track to achieve our dual mandate.	23	2
201506	1998	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	The markets place the likelihood of raising rates in September as roughly a coin flip.	23	2
201506	1999	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	We should do nothing to indicate higher odds.	23	2
201506	2000	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	We still need to see further improvement in economic conditions, and I currently expect those conditions to be met sometime after our September meeting.	23	2
201506	2001	2015-06-17	meeting	ROSENGREN	In terms of the areas that the Chair has asked us to discuss, I agree that a separate note on operational tools absolutely makes sense, and I think we should do it.	23	2

201506	2038	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Much of the apparent weakness in measured first-quarter GDP growth reflected the effects of transitory factors, including residual seasonality.	23	2
201506	2039	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	The recent strength of the data, including the retail sales data and employment data, reaffirm my view that we are on a solid trajectory with good momentum, and I expect we’ll reach full employment later this year across a wide variety of measures of labor market conditions.	23	2
201506	2040	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Inflation remains too low, however, and while I’m becoming more confident that inflation will resume its approach to our 2 percent target, we’ve been repeatedly disappointed in the past.	23	2
201506	2041	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	As a result, gathering more evidence that inflation is on the right trajectory seems warranted at this stage.	23	2
201506	2042	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	That said, I remain convinced that the time for liftoff is fast approaching and that waiting much longer to raise the federal funds rate risks falling behind the curve.	23	2
201506	2043	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Doing so could ultimately necessitate steeper rate increases after liftoff, which may confuse and disrupt markets here and across the globe.	23	2
201506	2044	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Of course, I understand that our liftoff is a discrete adjustment and one that’s difficult to undertake because of the concern that our actions may prove premature.	23	2
201506	2045	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Actually, I never even thought about this as pulling a tooth.	23	2

201506	2048	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	But as President Rosengren appropriately said, we can point to numerous cases in the past where other central banks tightened policy too quickly, leading to undesirable outcomes.	23	2
201506	2049	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	That said, it is important to remind ourselves that our economic fundamentals are much sounder and our policy stance much more accommodative than in those instances.	23	2
201506	2050	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Looking ahead to potential future policy statements and the issue of forward guidance, there are two issues of forward guidance on which we want to be clear.	23	2

201506	2055	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In paragraph 3, it says “The Committee currently anticipates that the economy will evolve in a manner that warrants a gradual increase in the target range for the federal funds rate” and has the other language about low interest rates.	23	2
201506	2056	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think this is an interesting topic about whether we want to introduce in the future some forward guidance of that type, the “gradual increase.”	23	2

201506	2058	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	I also think that there is the issue that I just mentioned, that the longer we wait to start liftoff, the less likely it is that it will be appropriate to have a gradual increase in the target range of the funds rate.	23	2
201506	2059	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	So I do see the choice of language in the future depending obviously on how long it is until we start liftoff.	23	2
201506	2060	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	If we do it sooner, then I think that would support a gradual increase in the target range.	23	2
201506	2061	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	If we wait significantly longer, then I think that that would not be quite appropriate.	23	2
201506	2062	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of the memo on monetary policy implementation and directives, I’m fully supportive of the approach and the language you mentioned, Madam Chair, and that is described in the memo.	23	2
201506	2063	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	It is good to distinguish clearly between monetary policy decisions and what I would call the technicalities needed to achieve those decisions.	23	2
201506	2064	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	And I think it’s also important that, as the memo notes, this distinction would allow for modest adjustments in implementation, if needed, without necessitating additional FOMC statements.	23	2
201506	2065	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	This ensures that we avoid sending an incorrect signal to the public that monetary policy has somehow changed when actually we’re just making a technical implementation adjustment.	23	2
201506	2066	2015-06-17	meeting	WILLIAMS	Regarding the directive, I agree with your comments, Madam Chair, that it could go either way, but I do tend to lean toward not wanting to put new directive language in this time just out of nervousness that we’re signaling that we’re preparing something, that it might be misinterpreted.	23	2

201506	2070	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans.	23	2
201506	2071	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201506	2072	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	To start, I support the plans for separate communication regarding our policy implementation tools after liftoff.	23	2
201506	2073	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	And I am okay with the housekeeping changes, but I can go either way, just as you suggested.	23	2
201506	2074	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	For today’s decision, I support alternative B as written.	23	2
201506	2075	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	I would note, though, that the recent softer economic data and lack of improvement in core PCE have led me to push back my preferred appropriate monetary policy liftoff date to midyear 2016.	23	2
201506	2076	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	My staff’s DSGE analysis that I talked about yesterday also pushed me in that direction.	23	2
201506	2077	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	As you recall, that analysis showed how changes in the Survey of Professional Forecasters’ 10-year CPI inflation outlook and other incoming data are holding back the model’s longer-run inflation outlook.	23	2
201506	2078	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	I appreciated the extremely useful and timely Tealbook analysis of the potential downward influences on the long-run equilibrium real interest rate and the policy implications of a lower value for r*.	23	2
201506	2079	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	I think most of us are accustomed to simply having a single r* assessment in mind and not really considering the uncertainty surrounding r*, at least as we formulate the models and analytical analyses.	23	2
201506	2080	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	A fundamental underpinning for the Committee’s choice of a 2 percent inflation objective back in January 2012 was strong confidence that the long-run equilibrium real rate was 2 percent or higher.	23	2
201506	2081	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Indeed, in our January 2012 SEP submissions, 16 out of 17 of the long-run federal funds rate dots were consistent with r* being between 2 and 2½ percent.	23	2
201506	2082	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Today the Tealbook assumes r* is 1½ percent, in line with its lower assessment for productivity growth and potential output growth.	23	2
201506	2083	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	And the Committee’s June SEP submissions show broad agreement on this point, as all but three of the long-run nominal funds rate dots are consistent with an equilibrium real rate between 1¼ and 1¾ percent.	23	2
201506	2084	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Furthermore, there is substantial uncertainty over this assessment.	23	2
201506	2085	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Larry Summers and Ben Bernanke have debated whether a lower equilibrium rate reflects secular stagnation or a persistent global savings glut, but quantifying the magnitudes of these factors remains an important research objective.	23	2
201506	2086	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Personally, I think that ascribing a zero effect to these phenomena seems unlikely.	23	2
201506	2087	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	More directly, lower potential output growth also suggests a lower r*.	23	2
201506	2088	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Again, the magnitude is uncertain and depends on the longer-run path for capital deepening, the effects of demographic trends, and whether TFP growth has persistently reverted to the slow-growth era of 1975 through 1995.	23	2
201506	2089	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Yesterday President Lacker made an interesting comment when he pointed out that the interest rate policy rules that we consider have intercepts and error terms that are isomorphic.	23	2
201506	2090	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	You can’t just, by themselves, pick out the contribution because they enter in a linear fashion.	23	2
201506	2091	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Okay.	23	2
201506	2092	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	But there is more identifying information that can come from these other analyses, like this list of factors that I just mentioned, and I think that it is important to assess that additional information as opposed to just ignoring it.	23	2
201506	2093	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	We should take into account the fact that the posterior distribution of long-run r* is widely dispersed and that most of the weight in this distribution is on lower values than we were thinking back in January 2012.	23	2
201506	2094	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Perhaps the posterior mode for r* is at the Tealbook assessment of 1½ percent.	23	2
201506	2095	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	But for me, 1 percent or below also garners significant weight, and I put far less weight on r* being as high as 2 percent and negligible weights on higher values above 2 percent.	23	2
201506	2096	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	This uncertainty has profound implications for monetary policy.	23	2
201506	2097	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	If the long-run equilibrium real rate is substantially lower than 2 percent, then the historically low nominal funds rate paths that most of us have written down in our SEP submissions are not nearly as accommodative as we might have previously thought.	23	2
201506	2098	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	And, Madam Chair, you alluded to the same phenomenon when you talked about if productivity growth ends up being slower, that means r* will be lower, and, in fact, each and every point of our funds rate settings will be more restrictive.	23	2
201506	2099	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Of course, if economic fundamentals improve strongly, and inflation begins to rise more quickly, I would see that as evidence that the lowest r* values are diminishing in likelihood.	23	2
201506	2100	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	And, you know, this is another refutable implication of the viewpoint I think President Lacker associated with, which is that high r* is quite possible.	23	2
201506	2101	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	In that case, our funds rate would be more accommodative and we ought to see inflation rising much more rapidly to our inflation objective.	23	2
201506	2102	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	That ends up being a testable implication, and we can look for that.	23	2
201506	2103	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	But I suspect that won’t be the case.	23	2
201506	2104	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	Most likely, the economy will continue to face many challenging headwinds.	23	2
201506	2105	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	I will look to the data in order to decide these issues, but I want to be clear that the data have already provided a lot of evidence suggesting troubling and highly persistent phenomena that should weigh importantly in our strategies concerning liftoff and the subsequent normalization of policy rates.	23	2
201506	2106	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	And just to be completely clear, I think that a full-throated endorsement of our symmetric inflation objective strategy could be a very helpful counterbalance to current and future headwinds.	23	2
201506	2107	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	I agree completely with the comments that President Kocherlakota made yesterday regarding risks to our inflation objective and how we should address them.	23	2
201506	2108	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	After all, even a 2 percent inflation target gives us uncomfortably little margin to engineer low enough real rates.	23	2
201506	2109	2015-06-17	meeting	EVANS	We don’t want to make things worse by creating a de facto target below 2 percent.	23	2
