201506	2112	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	First Vice President Holcomb.	23	2
201506	2113	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201506	2114	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	In reviewing the policy options in preparation for this meeting, one of our economists posited that we may find ourselves in a situation like that faced by the game warden in the movie Jurassic Park.	23	2
201506	2115	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	You may recall the scene in which the warden calmly and deliberately prepares to shoot an approaching velociraptor, only to discover too late that another raptor has snuck up on his flank.	23	2
201506	2116	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	His last words are “clever girl.”	23	2
201506	2117	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	[Laughter]	23	2
201506	2118	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	High inflation is the velociraptor that captures our attention as we watch for the right moment to deploy our weapons.	23	2
201506	2119	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	It is still quite far in the distance.	23	2
201506	2120	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Of greater or equal concern should be the raptor that may be sneaking up on our flank, the raptor that could bring this expansion to a premature or unpleasant end.	23	2
201506	2121	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	The worry is that business investment decisions, consumer durable goods purchases, and household and business borrowing commitments undertaken in an artificially favorable financial environment won’t be easily unwound when financial conditions eventually normalize.	23	2
201506	2122	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	It is difficult to achieve smooth convergence in an economy with capital and debt overhangs, and the longer artificially favorable financial conditions persist, the greater these overhangs are likely to become.	23	2
201506	2123	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	The damage to the economy from overshooting full employment is cumulative, and as it accumulates, the threat to macroeconomic stability mounts.	23	2
201506	2124	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	In other words, the price to be paid for running the economy hot is not just the risk of a period of above-target inflation.	23	2
201506	2125	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Even if inflation does not pick up, imbalances are created that are unsustainable.	23	2
201506	2126	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Consequently, the risks associated with too much and too little policy accommodation are not asymmetric as the economy approaches full employment.	23	2
201506	2127	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Too much accommodation or accommodation maintained far too long is as risky as too little accommodation, even after factoring in the zero lower bound for interest rates.	23	2
201506	2128	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	I noted yesterday that the Federal Reserve Bank of Dallas’ staff economic forecasts are generally in the central tendency of the projections submitted in this round of the SEP exercise.	23	2
201506	2129	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	They see the economy pushing past full employment early next year, and inflation, as measured by the Dallas Fed trimmed mean PCE index, reaching 2 percent by the end of 2016.	23	2
201506	2130	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	This is a different outlook than is presented in Tealbook, Book A, and, accordingly, we take a somewhat different view of the policy rule prescriptions in simulations presented in Tealbook B.	23	2
201506	2131	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Also, for reasons just discussed, we do not see the zero bound as a compelling reason for treating policy risk as asymmetric in an economy that is closing in on full employment.	23	2
201506	2132	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Accordingly, our view is that the appropriate path for the funds rate is likely to be steeper than is currently expected by the public or is assumed in the Tealbook baseline forecast.	23	2
201506	2133	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	We assess recent developments as providing reassurance that the risk of inflation running persistently below 2 percent has diminished.	23	2
201506	2134	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	So I lean toward alternative C.	23	2
201506	2135	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	It best describes our view of the data as the data have evolved since our April meeting, as well as the data’s implications for the outlook and appropriate policy.	23	2
201506	2136	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	However, I will support B, as it keeps our options open to respond to new data.	23	2
201506	2137	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	We have some concern, though, that B has the potential to mislead the public.	23	2
201506	2138	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	According to the SEP package, the majority of participants believes that it will be appropriate to raise the federal funds target range in September of 2015 or earlier.	23	2
201506	2139	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	This indicates substantially greater probability of liftoff by September than after September.	23	2
201506	2140	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	That is not what the private analysts think, according to the charts presented yesterday.	23	2
201506	2141	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Therefore, communications that help bring public perceptions more in line with those of the Committee will be important.	23	2
201506	2142	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	In response to the request yesterday, I have a couple of comments on alternative C′.	23	2
201506	2143	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	First, in paragraph 3, I think it is preferable not to include the statement that “the Committee currently anticipates that the economy will evolve in a manner that warrants a gradual increase in the target range for the federal funds rate,” even if it is true.	23	2
201506	2144	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	It is my understanding that the federal funds rate path prescribed by optimal control techniques and simple Taylor-style policy rules are quite sensitive to financial conditions and the economic outlook, so that the warranted policy rate path could steepen in response to completely plausible changes in circumstances.	23	2
201506	2145	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Saying that the Committee expects a gradual policy rate path without also communicating the substantial sensitivity of that expectation to changes in the outlook could give private decisionmakers a distorted view of how policy may evolve.	23	2
201506	2146	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	If the statement remains, a stronger warning about the degree to which normalization’s pace will be subject to adjustment as the economic outlook changes should also be included.	23	2
201506	2147	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Overall, we prefer to let private analysts draw their own inferences about the future path of policy from the SEP dot chart.	23	2
201506	2148	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	It also seems confusing in paragraph 4 to indicate that reinvesting principal and rolling over maturing Treasuries is designed to “help maintain accommodative financial conditions” in the same communication that conveys the Committee’s decision to reduce accommodation.	23	2
201506	2149	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	It would be better to make reference to or include the pertinent language from the Committee’s Policy Normalization Principles and Plans, which states that reinvestments will continue until later in the normalization process.	23	2
201506	2150	2015-06-17	meeting	HOLCOMB	Finally, with respect to the proposals on communicating the details for implementation at liftoff, I think the proposal presented is very sensible, and I support proceeding as described.	23	2

201506	2199	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	23	2
201506	2200	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201506	2201	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I support option B for today.	23	2
201506	2202	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	As I said yesterday and I’ve said in the past, with regard to our goal variables, we’re about as close as we’ve ever been in the postwar era.	23	2
201506	2203	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	So I think it’s time that we look for opportunities to move our target policy rate off emergency settings.	23	2
201506	2204	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	We have a zero policy rate, and we have a very large balance sheet.	23	2
201506	2205	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Those are the same settings that we had when we were much further from our goal variables.	23	2
201506	2206	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Certainly, the data that come in over the summer are going to be mixed, and I think we have to have the idea that we’ll be opportunistic in our first policy move.	23	2
201506	2207	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Also, once we make the policy move, obviously we’re still going to be very accommodative.	23	2
201506	2208	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	We’re trying to hedge our bets in the direction of the economy getting more toward normal, so we’re trying to move policy more toward normal, but we’re still going to be very accommodative.	23	2
201506	2209	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	We would like to take opportunities to make these policy moves, and I would very much like to make the first move on the back of good news about the economy.	23	2
201506	2210	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Prescheduling September is going to work against this principle.	23	2
201506	2211	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I mean, maybe the data will come in great right before that meeting and that will be perfect, but life often doesn’t work out perfectly.	23	2
201506	2212	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Anything we can do to try to get to a more flexible approach in which every meeting is, ex ante, identical I think would be very helpful.	23	2
201506	2213	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I don’t think the Committee is really ready to think in terms of moving opportunistically, but that’s how we’re going to have to move over the normalization process.	23	2
201506	2214	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	The more we can, in our own minds, get toward that kind of an attitude, and then maybe get to a method that would actually implement that, I think would be helpful.	23	2
201506	2215	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I have two comments on the SEP.	23	2
201506	2216	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	One is about SEP paths being given according to an optimal policy assumption, and the second is about the horizon.	23	2
201506	2217	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	First, I think when we talk about the SEP, we need to clarify to people that the projections are put forward under an optimal policy assumption.	23	2
201506	2218	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	We might all be using different models.	23	2
201506	2219	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Within those different models, policy might be somewhat different, and so the various forecasts are not all made on the same basis.	23	2
201506	2220	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	They are not unconditional forecasts the way private-sector forecasts are, where the private- sector forecaster is also trying to forecast what this Committee will do and will give you an out- and-out forecast that you would then evaluate against mean-squared criterion or something like that.	23	2
201506	2221	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Here we’re saying, given the models we have, we’re putting something in under an optimal policy within that model.	23	2
201506	2222	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	So I’d appreciate it if we’d mention this when we talk about the SEP because I don’t think that they are the same thing as the unconditional forecasts given in the private sector.	23	2
201506	2223	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	For me, missing a rate rise means worse outcomes for the economy, according to the model that I’m using.	23	2
201506	2224	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	So if you miss the time when the model said you should have lifted off, then you’re going to get worse outcomes going forward than you otherwise could have achieved if you had raised rates earlier.	23	2
201506	2225	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	But given that you didn’t move, there’s some optimal policy going on from that point.	23	2
201506	2226	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Over the normalization phase, I think this effect will cause federal funds rate dot paths to shift because we’re not all exactly on the same timing schedule.	23	2
201506	2227	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	So you’ve got these dot paths shifting around.	23	2
201506	2228	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	That may not be indicating a change in the sentiment of the Committee as to where we are or what we need to do but is a detail of how the SEP is put together.	23	2
201506	2229	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	So I try to emphasize this.	23	2
201506	2230	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I know that it doesn’t go very far when I talk to people outside this Committee.	23	2
201506	2231	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I know that we all understand it here, but the SEP is a different object from the private-sector forecasts that are often cited.	23	2
201506	2232	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	The second comment on the SEP is that the horizon shifts through the year.	23	2
201506	2233	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	That’s something that we’ve always done, but I think it is kind of odd, and it warps the interpretation of the SEP compared with what it otherwise could be.	23	2
201506	2234	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	What people really want to know is, what’s your year-ahead outlook and your two-year-ahead outlook?	23	2
201506	2235	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	We should always be giving them a year-ahead outlook and a two-year-ahead outlook in a format that they can digest and see what we’re saying.	23	2
201506	2236	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	What’s happening is, you get a bad first quarter.	23	2
201506	2237	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	Well, everyone has to mark down their forecast for the year if that was unexpected, and then we all think that the future looks worse than we previously said, but that isn’t really what’s going on.	23	2
201506	2238	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	We’re saying that that was an unexpected shock, and that the next four quarters and the four quarters beyond that might look roughly the same as they did before, and so that we have not perhaps changed our views that much on how the economy is going to evolve going forward.	23	2
201506	2239	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	So if we could get to something like that in the SEP, it might be an improvement.	23	2
201506	2240	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I understand that that’s a little bit different from how, let’s say, the IMF would do it, or how other people would do it, but on the other hand, we’re trying to convey what our outlook is, given the data we have today, then going forward from here—four-quarter, eight-quarter horizons.	23	2
201506	2241	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	On the other questions about C′ and about the housekeeping changes, I was fine with what the staff proposed.	23	2
201506	2242	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I don’t have any further comments on that.	23	2
201506	2243	2015-06-17	meeting	BULLARD	I would be happy to do the housekeeping changes at this meeting if people feel like that would get that out of the way, so we didn’t have to do that at the time of the actual rate rise.	23	2

201506	2336	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201506	2337	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	I support alternative C as being consistent with the data-dependent policy and with the statement in the previous FOMC minutes that the Committee’s decision to begin normalizing policy would appropriately be determined on a meeting-by-meeting basis.	23	2
201506	2338	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	In terms of the criteria for liftoff, the March meeting minutes noted that further improvement in the labor market, stabilization of energy prices, and a leveling out of the foreign exchange value of the dollar would all be seen as helpful in establishing confidence that inflation would turn up.	23	2
201506	2339	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	Since March, we’ve seen progress around each of those criteria.	23	2
201506	2340	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	Employment growth has averaged 207,000 over the past three months, and broader indicators of labor market activity have registered similar improvement.	23	2
201506	2341	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	Readings on core PCE inflation have remained largely stable on a year-over-year basis since December.	23	2
201506	2342	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	And, since the April meeting, we’ve seen oil prices drift higher while the dollar has been relatively stable, which together give me confidence that transitory effects will dissipate.	23	2
201506	2343	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	In addition, our policy rules continue to point to higher rates, and the byproduct of our highly accommodative policy can be found in the incentives of searching for higher yield and the willingness to take on additional risk when interest rate expectations are flat.	23	2
201506	2344	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	With the combination of these factors, and understanding that monetary policy operates with long lags, I believe that it is time to begin the process for normalizing policy.	23	2
201506	2345	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	In light of yesterday’s discussion about the implication of alternative values of the long- run federal funds rate, I would note, as I did at the previous meeting, that measures of r* often do not move independently of measures of the output gap.	23	2
201506	2346	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	I understand the correlation may not be perfect, but I think an important scenario to consider, as others have noted, is what a lower r*, driven by lower potential output, implies for monetary policy.	23	2
201506	2347	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	Productivity growth has been running far below earlier trends.	23	2
201506	2348	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	This suggests a low r* is likely to be reflective of slowing growth of potential GDP rather than persistent weak demand.	23	2
201506	2349	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	If that’s true, the implications for the output gap and liftoff do not necessarily suggest a later liftoff, so I look forward to further discussion and analysis of this aspect of our policy decisionmaking.	23	2
201506	2350	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	In terms of today’s decision, market expectations for liftoff are clearly focused on September, with a skew toward December and even into 2016.	23	2
201506	2351	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	This suggests to me that one soft data point—a soft employment report, similar to what we had in March—could easily push expectations back to December.	23	2
201506	2352	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	Yet for all the hand-wringing about the slowdown in Q1, the employment numbers remained solid and growth seems to be on a relatively firm footing.	23	2
201506	2353	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	Yet the strong employment report in May did little to move expectations forward.	23	2
201506	2354	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	This asymmetry is going to be hard to overcome, and it risks pushing back the date of liftoff as we wait to see a consistent streak of strong data.	23	2
201506	2355	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	In terms of the two items that we’ve highlighted, I am fine with a separate implementation note.	23	2
201506	2356	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	I think that will serve us well in keeping that separate from the statement.	23	2
201506	2357	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	And in terms of the housekeeping changes for the directive, I would be comfortable doing those today with the minutes, noting what their relevance is in terms of future decisions.	23	2
201506	2358	2015-06-17	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you.	23	2
201506	2359	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201506	2360	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	President Lacker.	23	2
201506	2361	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201506	2362	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	In April I noted that more than the usual amount of data was scheduled to come in by this meeting, and that, if it came in consistent with our projections, I thought a strong case could be made to raise the funds rate target.	23	2
201506	2363	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	To me, it’s clear that the data have been pretty consistent with our April expectations.	23	2
201506	2364	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	In fact, in the Tealbook projection for the first half, real GDP growth is now one-tenth higher than it was at the previous meeting.	23	2
201506	2365	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	It is also now apparent that we’re in the midst of the longest sustained improvement in household spending growth we’ve seen in this recovery.	23	2
201506	2366	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Labor market conditions have clearly improved as well.	23	2
201506	2367	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	We’ve continued strong growth in employment and job openings, and since the April meeting, we’ve seen confirmation of the expected rebound in core inflation.	23	2
201506	2368	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	So I believe we have good reason to be confident that, barring further shocks, inflation will move back to our 2 percent target.	23	2
201506	2369	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Taking this all on board, my preference would be to raise rates at this meeting.	23	2
201506	2370	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Raising rates now would be a natural and understandable response to the economic data we have in hand, and a quarter-point increase would still leave us with a highly accommodative policy stance, a point Governor Fischer made eloquently last time.	23	2
201506	2371	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I will not vote against keeping rates unchanged today, however.	23	2
201506	2372	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I understand the concerns of those for whom the incoming data are not yet completely convincing, and I do not think we would be making a terribly costly mistake by waiting another meeting or two to raise rates.	23	2
201506	2373	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	It would raise the risk of getting behind the curve, but at this point, tolerably so, I think.	23	2
201506	2374	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I do believe that the risk would rise if the data come in in line with our projections over the next several months and we don’t raise rates.	23	2
201506	2375	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	In addition, I see risk going forward of our data dependence becoming something of a one-way ratchet mechanism, as described by President George, in which the emergence of new reasons for concern, soft data points, lead us to delay expected liftoff, but the dissipation or passing of those soft data points does not lead to a commensurate offsetting movement bringing the expected liftoff backward in time.	23	2
201506	2376	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Our data dependence ought to be symmetric in this respect.	23	2
201506	2377	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	More broadly, as we go into this, we should recognize that there are always going to be concerns.	23	2
201506	2378	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Soft data points will always turn up from time to time, and the prospect of certainty just around the corner is something of a mirage.	23	2
201506	2379	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Regarding the statement, I prefer the language of alternative C to that of alternative B.	23	2
201506	2380	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	President Mester was open about this.	23	2
201506	2381	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I think it better reflects reality right now.	23	2
201506	2382	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Any remaining underutilization of labor resources is immaterial, I believe, and I think that the risk of inflation running below 2 percent has diminished significantly.	23	2
201506	2383	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	More broadly, I support her concerns about the statement.	23	2
201506	2384	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	In particular, I’d highlight the reliance we’ve been placing lately on paragraph 1, which is a recitation of what has happened since the previous meeting, and I think that gives short shrift in the statement to the extent to which our decision is going to be driven by a longer-run perspective on what’s evolved in the economic data.	23	2
201506	2385	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	In addition, I don’t think we should view it as necessary that we send a message like statement C as a clear signal, as a prerequisite for liftoff.	23	2
201506	2386	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	So we shouldn’t wait.	23	2
201506	2387	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Liftoff should be a live option whether or not we’ve issued a statement like C.	23	2
201506	2388	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	And, commensurately, a statement like C shouldn’t make us feel compelled to lift off at the next meeting.	23	2
201506	2389	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I think that’s consistent with the extent to which we’ve decided to make decisions on a meeting-by-meeting, data-dependent basis.	23	2
201506	2390	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Regarding alternative C′, I think we should give some very careful thought to the sentence in paragraph 3 that talks about “a gradual increase in the target range.”	23	2
201506	2391	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I share some of the concerns that have been expressed about this.	23	2
201506	2392	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	This reintroduces forward guidance language, and it’s language that’s awfully reminiscent of the measured-pace formula that I was a party to from 2004 to 2006.	23	2
201506	2393	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	In hindsight, I’m not sure that that was a good idea, and my sense is that there are widely shared misgivings ex post about that.	23	2
201506	2394	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Maybe it didn’t absolutely lock us in to moving 25 basis points every single meeting, but it did seem to raise a bar that made it hard to do anything but 25 basis points.	23	2
201506	2395	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	And I think the word “gradual” could suffer the same fate.	23	2
201506	2396	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	It could become identified with moving at every other meeting.	23	2
201506	2397	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	And our scheduled press conference at every other meeting is going to have this gravitational pull for us that could lead people to believe, “Well, ‘gradual’ means that at every other meeting they raise rates by 25 basis points.”	23	2
201506	2398	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	In addition, when we introduce new language, I think we ought to ask ourselves, what would cause us to pull it out?	23	2
201506	2399	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Would it be easy to remove when we thought it was inappropriate, or would we be afraid of being misread by pulling it out?	23	2
201506	2400	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I think we would be afraid that it would be over-interpreted as a very high probability for us moving very rapidly very soon, and I’m not sure that makes sense.	23	2
201506	2401	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	So I think this deserves a lot of careful thought.	23	2
201506	2402	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Another broad comment on language:  I don’t think we should be focusing on 12-month inflation numbers.	23	2
201506	2403	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	For example, if the monthly numbers came in pretty strong for a few months, I don’t think it would make sense for us to stubbornly insist on waiting for the 12-month number to shed the low numbers we saw at the end of last year.	23	2
201506	2404	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I think we should be focusing on the monthly numbers as much as the 12-month number.	23	2
201506	2405	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	About the operational note, I think it is a great idea.	23	2
201506	2406	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	For the directive, I agree with Governor Brainard and President Williams that we should wait until liftoff to make changes.	23	2
201506	2407	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	And, in particular, I’d say if we’re going to do some housekeeping on the directive, the thing that really stands out is this sentence that reads, “The Committee directs the Desk to undertake open market operations as necessary to maintain such conditions.”	23	2
201506	2408	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I mean, this is an archaic vestige of a previous regime.	23	2
201506	2409	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	We don’t anticipate they’re going to need to undertake open market operations to maintain reserves markets consistent with the funds rate trading in the range—we don’t think that’s going to happen.	23	2
201506	2410	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	So it’s this confusing vestige of a previous regime.	23	2
201506	2411	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	I’d urge the staff to take a much more fundamental and far-reaching look at the directive, its structure, and what it says.	23	2
201506	2412	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	It has been this highly coded kind of semaphore to markets and to the more sophisticated Fed watchers in the markets for decades.	23	2
201506	2413	2015-06-17	meeting	LACKER	Maybe it’s time to start from scratch on this.	23	2

201506	2417	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I support option B, which does a well-crafted job of indicating that we have made further progress toward our goals.	23	2
201506	2418	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	We have not yet reached them, but we are very close.	23	2
201506	2419	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	As I noted yesterday, I am reasonably optimistic about near-term economic activity, particularly in the labor market, and about near- to medium-term inflation.	23	2
201506	2420	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I am, therefore, hopeful that we will soon be able to put in place a decision reflecting language like that we have in option C′.	23	2
201506	2421	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	As Mike Kiley noted in his box in the Tealbook, and as Jim Bullard has mentioned twice, the economy is closer to our goals now than it has been at just about any time over the past 50 years.	23	2
201506	2422	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	This helps explain why Taylor rules with no inertia indicate that the federal funds rate is far too low.	23	2
201506	2423	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	But at this point, the other rules shown in Tealbook B are also in agreement that it is about time to begin normalization.	23	2
201506	2424	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	While I know it is possible to devise new rules—say, with lower equilibrium real rates, which would delay normalization further—that kind of reverse engineering strikes me as risky.	23	2
201506	2425	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Now, of course, most economic models are not going to make a big deal of a 25 basis point move, so it is hard to argue forcefully about the perfect moment to move rates.	23	2
201506	2426	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	But, to my mind, there are two additional reasons for getting things started soon.	23	2
201506	2427	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	First, I believe that if the FOMC sends a well-reasoned signal that we think the US economy is now strong enough to begin normalizing, that could be an important boost to confidence for businesses and households.	23	2
201506	2428	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Seven or eight years is a very long time to be proclaiming, by our decisions, that we are in a recession or a crisis of some sort.	23	2
201506	2429	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Such an improvement in confidence would have a positive effect on spending and job creation.	23	2
201506	2430	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Second—and this is something that I think President Williams mentioned in other language—I think that beginning normalization in the next couple of meetings, when we have met the criteria that we have set out to meet, will enhance the credibility of the Federal Reserve.	23	2
201506	2431	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Conversely, I think that if we continue to delay, market participants and Fed watchers won’t know what to make of our communications.	23	2
201506	2432	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I would like to go on to a couple of topics raised by yesterday’s discussion.	23	2
201506	2433	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Let me mention one that I think we need to discuss at greater length shortly.	23	2
201506	2434	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	The story about other central banks that raised rates and then had to reduce them is not actually accurate.	23	2
201506	2435	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	The Swedes are very angry that we keep quoting that, and I am guilty of the same sin.	23	2
201506	2436	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	When the economy was recovering and the inflation rate was high, we raised the interest rate in Israel.	23	2
201506	2437	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	When the European crisis began, we reduced it.	23	2
201506	2438	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	They were both appropriate, so I don’t understand what the argument is about—and I assure you that there is going to be a day, whenever we raise interest rates, that we will one day reduce them, and people will say, “Ha.	23	2
201506	2439	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	You raised them too soon.”	23	2
201506	2440	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	But there is a serious discussion to take place, and we ought to do it, Madam Chair, at some point.	23	2
201506	2441	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Thomas also asked us yesterday whether the language in alternative C′, particularly paragraph 3, is acceptable.	23	2
201506	2442	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	My answer is “Yes,” because there is a lot in there about what we will change.	23	2
201506	2443	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Whether it will be gradual or not depends on how the data come in.	23	2
201506	2444	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	That is, it is consistent with data dependence.	23	2
201506	2445	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	In his notes, Thomas referred to this framework of paragraph 3 as providing forward guidance.	23	2
201506	2446	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I don’t think it is forward guidance, and I don’t think so for a reason that I can make clear in this forum.	23	2
201506	2447	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I once heard a senior Federal Reserve official say, “We have two instruments now that we are at the zero lower bound.	23	2
201506	2448	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	One is quantitative easing, and the other is forward guidance.”	23	2
201506	2449	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I said, “But forward guidance must be consistent with your predictions for the interest rate and for what you are going to do on quantitative easing.”	23	2
201506	2450	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	And the answer I got was, “No, it’s an extra instrument.”	23	2
201506	2451	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	It is not an extra instrument.	23	2
201506	2452	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	And I think forward guidance is not providing information about what we think we will do, based on our current knowledge and our current expectations.	23	2
201506	2453	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Rather, it is that there are things we will do in the future, which, because we announce them today, we will do despite the fact that we don’t think they are optimal from the viewpoint of the future.	23	2
201506	2454	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	That is, there are binding commitments that we have entered into in forward guidance that are inconsistent with data dependence, and that, I think, is the difference.	23	2
201506	2455	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	So I don’t think of this as forward guidance; it is not consistent with forward guidance as that term has begun to be used in the economic literature, and as it has been used in the FOMC’s past decisions.	23	2
201506	2456	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	One other point on C′.	23	2
201506	2457	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	In the past, we have discussed two strategies, “early and gradual” versus “late and steep.”	23	2
201506	2458	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	I believe we are now too late to be early, but fortunately I think we can now call what we are going to be doing “timely and probably gradual.”	23	2
201506	2459	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	With regard to the questions that were asked, a separate implementation note is preferable.	23	2
201506	2460	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	And I join those who don’t think we should make a change to the directive now and then make additional changes when we commence normalization.	23	2
201506	2461	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	So let me sum up.	23	2
201506	2462	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	The criteria for beginning normalization have nearly been met, and we should be willing to move very soon.	23	2
201506	2463	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Of course, we are data dependent.	23	2
201506	2464	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	And if the data falter again, or the economy gets hit by some significant new negative shock, we want to see how things unfold.	23	2
201506	2465	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	But I would also caution against interpreting every small weakness as a reason to push off normalization.	23	2
201506	2466	2015-06-17	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201506	2467	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201506	2468	2015-06-17	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Tarullo.	23	2
201506	2469	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201506	2470	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	I support alternative B with the language as drafted in the Tealbook.	23	2
201506	2471	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	I think that is a relatively straightforward decision for today.	23	2
201506	2472	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Looking forward and thinking about the two criteria that we have injected into our decisionmaking for an interest rate increase, I find myself again—as you can probably tell from my remarks yesterday—focused on the apparent breakdown in some of the traditional relationships, both in thinking about labor markets and between wages and price inflation.	23	2
201506	2473	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	I think that is posing—for me, at least—a challenge in trying to make a decision about when it would be appropriate to lift off for the first time.	23	2
201506	2474	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	With respect to further improvement in labor conditions, taken quite literally, one could say that that criterion had been met almost successively since we first put it in, since there has been some improvement at each step along the way.	23	2
201506	2475	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	But, obviously, the connotation at least is that the amount of improvement that people are looking for probably depends on the gap that they think exists and how much improvement remains to be done.	23	2
201506	2476	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	And so I think some of you indicate that you think we are very close to or maybe even at the natural rate already, and, therefore, you don’t think there is much room for further improvement.	23	2
201506	2477	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	I think President Lacker said any further improvement was immaterial.	23	2
201506	2478	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	So, obviously, if you take that view, it is easier to make a decision.	23	2
201506	2479	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	But if one is somewhat sympathetic, as I am, to some of the arguments that are made in some of the papers that I cited yesterday and have cited in the past—that there may be a nontrivial amount of slack left—then the amount of improvement that I may look to is somewhat greater.	23	2
201506	2480	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	With respect to reasonable confidence about inflation, I find that to be an even more slippery criterion to try to get my arms around in terms of making a decision on liftoff.	23	2
201506	2481	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Here I think most people are probably relying on a fairly widely shared intuition that the progressive removal of slack in the economy will at some point begin to push up inflation.	23	2
201506	2482	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	But that intuition—which may have been based on some elegant stuff that you all studied or wrote about when you were in graduate school or in the pre-crisis, pre-recession era—may have broken down to some extent, at least if the more recent literature can be believed.	23	2
201506	2483	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	And the Peneva-Rudd paper I cited yesterday was the latest in a string of research papers suggesting that that may be the case.	23	2
201506	2484	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Now, why is that important to me?	23	2
201506	2485	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Well, it is important because even though I think we all agree that further removal of slack in the economy—as imperfectly reflected in the tightening of labor market conditions—should translate into upward pressure on inflation at some point, the “how much” and “when” actually matter a good deal.	23	2
201506	2486	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	And if we no longer have a kind of reasonably well-understood relationship between the progression of wages and the progression of prices, then it makes it a more difficult judgment.	23	2
201506	2487	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	So if, for example, it were a longer period of time that it took for tighter labor markets and rising wages to translate into price inflation, that would mean there would be a longer period during which exogenous shocks of some sort might adversely affect the economy.	23	2
201506	2488	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	And so I might be more concerned that moving more quickly would put the economy at some risk and not be necessary, really, to stave off inflation.	23	2
201506	2489	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Now, that can go in the other direction as well.	23	2
201506	2490	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	As I think President Williams pointed out a meeting or two ago, when you break that relationship, and you don’t have something to substitute for it, it may be that price inflation could begin to be apparent even in the absence of demonstrable growth in nominal wages.	23	2
201506	2491	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	And the reasonable confidence people may have could take root a little bit more quickly, even in the absence of higher nominal wage growth.	23	2
201506	2492	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	But I do find it a bit disconcerting to have not even a rough calibration of “when” and “how much” is necessary in order to induce that reasonable confidence.	23	2
201506	2493	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	As President Williams said yesterday, it is hard to avoid the recognition that we keep falling short on the inflation target.	23	2
201506	2494	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	I guess that has affected the way I am thinking about liftoff.	23	2
201506	2495	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	But precisely because there isn’t a nice linear relationship to fit any of this into, it doesn’t predetermine the position I will have in September, or any later meeting, for that matter.	23	2
201506	2496	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	With regard to the issues that have been raised, as I have said in the past, I hope we rely principally on paragraphs 1 and 2 to communicate future intentions.	23	2
201506	2497	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	I agree with those who think that we shouldn’t be relying simply on the recitation of the past, which is paragraph 1.	23	2
201506	2498	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	Stating where we expect the economy to go, which is what paragraph 2 is about, should provide some measure of signal and communication to markets so that they can then adjust their assessments of how soon we are likely to move.	23	2
201506	2499	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	What has always made me a bit nervous about changes in paragraph 3 is my “kitchen timer” analogy, that making a change in paragraph 3 gets people to think, okay, it’s one meeting or it’s two meetings from now.	23	2
201506	2500	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	I will say that, on that scale, the insertion of “some” to characterize the degree of labor market improvement would not be the worst offender.	23	2
201506	2501	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	There have been things proposed in the past which I think would have been worse.	23	2
201506	2502	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	But I would still tend to shy away from it a little bit.	23	2
201506	2503	2015-06-17	meeting	TARULLO	I am sympathetic to what President Kocherlakota said about how it would be better if we had a somewhat more precise set of criteria in paragraph 3, but I fear that trying to make that change now would just result in more confusion rather than more clarity.	23	2

201506	2515	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	“Exhibit A” for that would be the significant markdown in 2015 growth since the March SEP.	23	2
201506	2516	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	And I think the market is right not to expect us to act here.	23	2
201506	2517	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	On the other hand, the more recent improvement in data makes September liftoff a plausible thing for me.	23	2
201506	2518	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	The Committee will recall that the actual taper, when it happened in December of 2013, was a non-event because it was in the market—not just in the literal sense of being predicted by the market, but, psychologically, it seemed accepted by market participants—so that no one took any inference about the Committee’s objective function.	23	2
201506	2519	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	If you look at the situation today with the first interest rate increase, the real story is the path forward.	23	2
201506	2520	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	And the market seems to have fully internalized that and accepted it, and I think we are reaching a point at which a liftoff in the latter part of this year would really raise no threat to the market’s understanding of a low path going forward.	23	2
201506	2521	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Indeed, the market’s understanding is it will be lower than the Committee says by a substantial margin, albeit a diminishing one.	23	2
201506	2522	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	So I guess I think we are reaching a point at which a 25 basis point increase wouldn’t be that important and would not have broad implications.	23	2
201506	2523	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	So my SEP path is for September liftoff with another increase in December, 25 basis points each, and then averaging 25 basis points every other meeting, although I don’t mean to imply that we should get on an escalator with equally spaced steps.	23	2
201506	2524	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Both market readings and surveys show an expectation that there is about a 40 percent chance of liftoff in September.	23	2
201506	2525	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	That feels about right to me.	23	2
201506	2526	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	I think the Committee’s two conditions for liftoff, as set forth in the statement and amplified and sketched out in more detail by the Chair, are nearly fulfilled.	23	2
201506	2527	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	There has been further improvement in the labor market.	23	2
201506	2528	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	And to address the point raised by Governor Tarullo, I have been thinking about that and talking about that as meaning a material diminution or diminishment of slack.	23	2
201506	2529	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	So, you know, a tenth here and there is really not enough.	23	2
201506	2530	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	You want to see slack coming out of the market in a material way, and I think that has been met with more than 200,000 in monthly job growth this year.	23	2
201506	2531	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	We have also had a firm participation rate for more than a year and a half now and a modest upward move in wages.	23	2
201506	2532	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	My confidence that inflation will move back to 2 percent in the medium term has been strengthened by the continuing tightening in the economy.	23	2
201506	2533	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	The two factors that we know are distorting inflation readings, the exchange value of the dollar and the price of oil, seem to have stabilized for now.	23	2
201506	2534	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Signs that wages are increasing continue to accumulate gradually but steadily.	23	2
201506	2535	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	The risk of a real weakening of inflation expectations has not materialized.	23	2
201506	2536	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Survey measures are stable.	23	2
201506	2537	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Longer-term breakevens have climbed above their lows of earlier this year as spot oil prices have increased.	23	2
201506	2538	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	I would add a couple of thoughts as well on the discussion that we had at the end of yesterday’s meeting.	23	2
201506	2539	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Obviously, it is appropriate to try to avoid surprising the market, and I would not like to see the market move in the next six or eight weeks to downgrade significantly the possibility of a September liftoff unless, of course, that is due to incoming data.	23	2
201506	2540	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	If the data come in as expected, I would really like to see the Committee be able to keep its options open for September.	23	2
201506	2541	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	But looking back at the experience over the past few years, the taper tantrum was a surprise to me, and I think generally to the Committee, the staff, and the world.	23	2
201506	2542	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	It is also surprising that it appears to have left little or no mark on the economy.	23	2
201506	2543	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	And, by the way, neither did the fiscal cliff, and neither did the government shutdown, all of which happened in 2013, with 2013 being the only year in which the economy has reached 3 percent growth since the crisis.	23	2
201506	2544	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Now, many of you are probably thinking, “Well, but it should have been a 4 percent year,” and I would just say to that, “No.	23	2
201506	2545	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	I don’t think so.	23	2
201506	2546	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	I really don’t.”	23	2
201506	2547	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	As I mentioned, we had the actual taper at a meeting in which there were low odds of a taper happening, and it did invoke a big reaction, only the sign was wrong—it was a positive reaction.	23	2
201506	2548	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	Then, coming into 2014, everyone seemed to agree, and I certainly did, that rates would start to go up in 2014.	23	2
201506	2549	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	This was a no-brainer.	23	2
201506	2550	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	And then the opposite happened.	23	2
201506	2551	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	So what are the takeaways here?	23	2
201506	2552	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	First, it just is not possible to confidently predict the reaction of financial markets.	23	2
201506	2553	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	The markets will do what they will.	23	2
201506	2554	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	But, second, it is not at all clear that a little volatility or a 25 basis point or 50 basis point rate increase, even across the curve, will slow the United States economy down much.	23	2
201506	2555	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	It may be more painful for emerging market economies, but I would echo what President Williams said earlier.	23	2
201506	2556	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	There is so much focus around the world on this that one would think they are as ready as they can be.	23	2
201506	2557	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	A great CEO that I worked with for years used to always say, “Control the controllable.”	23	2
201506	2558	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	In this case, what the Committee controls is our decision, and, to a much smaller extent, our communication about that decision.	23	2
201506	2559	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	And I think we ought to make that decision on the merits and not worry excessively about the market reaction.	23	2
201506	2560	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	I wouldn’t go so far as to say ignore the bond market, as some have, but I would not let it drive the Committee’s decisions.	23	2

201506	2564	2015-06-17	meeting	POWELL	I think there is very little chance that an amended directive with just technical amendments that is echoed in the minutes dropped three weeks after this press conference and this meeting would be mistaken for some signal about the path of policy.	23	2

201506	2572	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	I believe there is value to watchful waiting while additional data help clarify the economy’s underlying momentum.	23	2
201506	2573	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	This value is heightened by the asymmetry of risk-management considerations.	23	2
201506	2574	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The combination of the statement and the SEP release conveys that approach nicely, I think.	23	2
201506	2575	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	As I discussed yesterday, the pace of economic improvement slowed at the beginning of the year, and it is as yet unclear how strong or persistent the forces holding back stronger growth are likely to be.	23	2
201506	2576	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The labor force participation rate and the share of employees working part time for economic reasons suggest that slack remains, although the strength of job openings, the recent reacceleration in payrolls, and some hopeful signs on wages suggest slack is diminishing at a good pace.	23	2
201506	2577	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In contrast, although inflation has rebounded from the low levels at the turn of the year, measures of core inflation remain stubbornly below our target, and not noticeably different from the average subpar pace of inflation over the recovery.	23	2
201506	2578	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	And the puzzling disconnect between tepid aggregate growth and stronger labor market improvement complicates our task.	23	2
201506	2579	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	With remaining slack, and inflation persistently below our target, it is important that reasonably robust increases in aggregate demand be maintained going forward to promote the further improvement in labor market conditions and the movement of inflation back toward 2 percent that are our conditions for liftoff.	23	2
201506	2580	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	The totality of data that we have received so far on economic activity in the first half raises some questions about the sufficiency of growth in demand and whether that growth will be maintained.	23	2
201506	2581	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	So I am not yet reasonably confident that we will soon achieve our targets.	23	2
201506	2582	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Moreover, uncertainty over Greek default is becoming more acute.	23	2
201506	2583	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	This raises the risk of market disruptions over the coming days and weeks.	23	2
201506	2584	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	That said, it is not difficult to imagine a flow of data over the next few months that would leave me reasonably confident, such that liftoff by September is appropriate.	23	2
201506	2585	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	However, if the data take longer to convince, October or December might look more compelling, while recognizing there are some special features in late December that require careful consideration, including light trading and year-end dynamics.	23	2
201506	2586	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	Separately, I am comfortable with the staff recommendation to issue, upon liftoff, a policy implementation note to accompany and complement the FOMC statement, which would separate the statement of monetary policy from the operational details necessary to implement that policy.	23	2
201506	2587	2015-06-17	meeting	BRAINARD	In addition, on balance, I would prefer not to undertake housekeeping changes to the directive at this time, as I don’t see any compelling benefit.	23	2

201506	2595	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In considering a September liftoff versus later, I would like to build on something that Governor Brainard brought up, a consideration that makes September more attractive to me—the fact that markets will be considerably thinner and more likely to be affected by balance sheet constraints in December compared with September.	23	2
201506	2596	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	So if it is a close call, I would much prefer to move in September rather than commence liftoff in December.	23	2
201506	2597	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	In my mind, a December liftoff would likely be sloppier because trading activity would be depressed.	23	2
201506	2598	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Trading desks would be thinly staffed, and balance sheet constraints would likely exert more of an effect at year-end than at other times.	23	2

201506	2601	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Well, I don’t think there’s anything wrong with October per se, but I think it’s really unlikely that we’re going to actually decide to lift off in a non-press-conference meeting, even though we’ve said that all meetings are live.	23	2
201506	2602	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	Why do I reach that conclusion?	23	2

201506	2604	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	To lift off at a non-press-conference meeting, you have to get sufficient news over the interval between the two meetings to get over that higher bar.	23	2

201506	2606	2015-06-17	meeting	DUDLEY	The data are unlikely to come in so one- sided to push the motivation up sufficiently to transition from “no” at a press conference meeting to “yes” at a non-press-conference meeting six or seven weeks later.	23	2
